title": "Bouquet garni",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Bouquet garni: Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#bouquetgarni #herbs #celery #parsley #thyme #leek #stock #rosemary #soup #beefbourguignon #bouquetgarniformutton \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=The bouquet garni (French for \"garnished bouquet\") is a bundle of herbs usually tied together with string and mainly used to prepare soup\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Bouquet garni.jpg|150px|thumb|right|A bouquet garni]]\nThe bouquet garni (French for \"garnished bouquet\") is a bundle of [[herbs]] usually tied together with string and mainly used to prepare [[soup]], [[stock]], and various [[stews]]. The bouquet is boiled (usually for a long time) with the other ingredients, but is removed prior to consumption.\n\nThere is no generic recipe for bouquet garni, but most recipes include [[parsley]], [[thyme]] and [[bay leaf]]. Depending on the recipe, the bouquet garni may include [[basil]], [[celery|celery leaves]], [[thyme]], [[chervil]], [[rosemary]], [[peppercorns]], [[savory]] and [[tarragon]]. Sometimes, [[vegetables]] such as [[carrot]], [[celery]], [[celery|celery root]], [[leek]], [[onion]] and [[Parsley|parsley root]], are also included in the bouquet.  For [[stock]] making, the most common [[herbs]] are [[thyme]], [[parsley]] and [[bay leaves]].\n\nOccasionally, the bouquet is not bound with string, and its ingredients are instead filled into a small sachet, a net, or even a tea strainer, when it is known as a [[Sachet d'\u00e9pices|sachet d'\u00e9pices]].\n\nTraditionally, the aromatics are bound within [[leek]] leaves, though a coffee filter or [[butcher's twine]]/[[kitchen string]] can be used in their place.\n\nDishes made with a bouquet garni include:\n* [[Beef Bourguignon]]\n* [[Pot au feu]]\n* [[Poule au pot]]\n* Carbonnade flamande\n* Lapin chasseur\n* [[Ossobuco]]\n* [[Bouillabaisse]]\n==See also==\nWe have a number of bouquets garni recipes tailored for specific dishes\n* [[Basic bouquet garni]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for beef]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for fish]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for game]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for lamb]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for mutton]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for pork]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for poultry]]\n* [[Bouquet garni for vegetables]]\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Herbs]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#bouquetgarni #herbs #celery #parsley #thyme #leek #stock #rosemary #soup #beefbourguignon #bouquetgarniformutton </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Breakfast waffles, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#breakfastwaffles #batter #vegetableoil #eggwhites #bakingpowder #breakfast #eggyolks #flour #griddled #miseenplace #freerangeeggs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=These basic breakfast waffles are simple and predictable to make\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 955\n|PortionCalories = 238\n|DatePublished=5th January 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  26 minutes\n|PrepTime =  8 minutes\n|CookTime =  18 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Breakfast waffles recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice, but not for breakfast!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Bacon and eggs is for breakfast!!!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThese basic [[Breakfast|breakfast]] [[Waffles|waffles]] are simple and predictable to make. The [[Batter|batter]] can be made in about 15 minutes, so they are suitable as a last-minute addition to a [[Breakfast|breakfast]]. They are made fluffy by beating the [[Egg whites|egg whites]] separately and folding them in as the last step.\n\nYou may find it easier to weight the liquids as 354ml of [[Milk|milk]] is roughly 354g, etc.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 [[free range eggs]], separated\n| 354 ml (1.5) cups [[Milk|milk]]\n| 225g (1/2 lb) ''approx. 1 &#190; cups' [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 60 ml (1/4 cup) [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Heat the waffle maker / waffle machine / waffle [[Iron|iron]]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] and [[Milk|milk]].\n| Add [[Flour|flour]], [[Baking powder|baking powder]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Salt|salt]] and mix well.\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]].\n| Beat the [[Egg whites|egg whites]] until stiff and then fold into the [[Batter|batter]].\n| Lightly [[Spray|spray]] the non-stick plates with [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]].\n| Pour about 1 cup of [[Batter|batter]] into the waffle maker and close the lid.\n| Close and cook until the lights indicate the waffle is cooked or until the waffle stops steaming - about 5 minutes.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* http://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Cookbook:Breakfast_Waffles\n==See also==\n\n* {{SeeAlso-Waffles}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belgian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#breakfastwaffles #batter #vegetableoil #eggwhites #bakingpowder #breakfast #eggyolks #flour #griddled #miseenplace #freerangeeggs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

either by wiping with a lightly oiled [[Paper towel|paper towel]] or by using an oil [[Spray|spray]]\n| Add a small ladle of [[Batter|batter]] and swirl the pan around to distribute the batter evenly\n| Once the underside has been lightly [[Browned|browned]] (about 2 minutes), flip with a spatula and cook for a further 2 minutes\n| Rinse and repeat, keeping the cooked [[Pancakes|pancakes]] warm in the [[Oven|oven]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n'''Sweet fillings'''\n* Sprinkle with [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n* [[Strawberries]] and [[Cream|cream]]\n* [[Nutella]] [[Chocolate spread|chocolate spread]]\n* [[Maple syrup]]\n* [[Golden syrup]]\n* [[Black treacle]]\n* [[Jam]]\n'''Savoury fillings'''\n* [[Grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]]\n* Chopped [[Ham|ham]] and [[Scrambled eggs|scrambled eggs]]\n* Chopped [[Boiled eggs|boiled eggs]]\n* Cooked [[Spinach|spinach]]\n* [[Bacon]] and [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]]\n===Chef's notes===\nThey can be made ahead of time and reheated by [[Steaming|steaming]] or microwaving. In this case, separate each [[Pancake|pancake]] with [[greaseproof paper]] to prevent them sticking together.\n==See also==\n* [[Traditional English pancakes]]\n* [[Cr\u00eape recipe]]\n* [[Potato pancakes]]\n* [[Crispy duck pancake recipe]]\n* [[Crispy potato pancakes]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just need to find my beret</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Reminds me of our Aquitaine holidays, back in my surfing days.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pancakes #bretonbuckwheatpancakes #buckwheatflour #batter #frying #plainflour #tablesalt #nutella #crepe #blacktreacle #traditionalenglishpancakes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It has a dark, golden, and flaky crust from an [[egg wash]] applied before and after [[Proofing|proofing]].\n\n'''[[Dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 teaspoons [[Dried active yeast|dried active yeast]]\n| 420 g [[Strong white flour|strong white flour]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 100 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 3 medium [[Eggs|eggs]]\n| 70 ml [[Milk|milk]]\n}}\n'''[[Egg]] wash'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 medium [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6).\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the ingredients to your breadmaker in the above order.\n| Set to your [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] to Basic [[Dough]] (no [[Bake|bake]]) setting.\n| Use menu 16 ''Basic dough'' (2 hours 20 minutes) on [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]]\n| Place the [[Dough|dough]] in a greased bowl, cover and leave to rest in a [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] for 30 minutes.\n| Dust a worktop with [[flour]] and divide the [[Dough|dough]] into 12 equal portions.\n| From each portion make two balls, one large, one small.Place each large ball into a greased brioche or [[Muffin|muffin]] cup, dimple the top with a floured thumb and place the small ball into the indent.\n| Cover and leave to rise in a [[warm place]] (30\u00b0 C) for 30 minutes.\n| [[Brush]] with a beaten [[Egg|egg]].\n| [[Bake]] for 10 to 15 minutes until golden [[Brown|brown]].\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#brioche #egg #dough #bake #butter #breadmaker #eggs #crumb #flour #warmplace #driedactiveyeast </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cauliflower soup with Green Tapenade a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cauliflower #thyme #garlic #onion #parsley #boil #soup #cream #butter #tapenade #cauliflowersoupwithgreentapenade \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another vegetarian offering for our Gent night\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1376\n|PortionCalories = 229\n|DatePublished=22nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Belazu tapenade.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Ahh, Ghent Nights!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fabulous city, well worth a visit.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother [[vegetarian]] offering for our [http://www.guardian.co.uk/lifeandstyle/wordofmouth/2009/may/14/ghent-vegetarian-city-healthy-belgium Gent night]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 large [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] \n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]] \n| 1 [[Garlic|garlic]] clove \n| 25 g [[Butter|butter]] \n| 2-3 sprigs [[Thyme|thyme]] \n| 1.4 [[Litres|litres]] [[Chicken|chicken]] or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] \n| 100g [[gruy\u00e8re cheese]]\n| Small bunch of [[Flat-leaf parsley|flat-leaf parsley]] \n| 150ml [[Cream|cream]] or [[Milk|milk]] \n| 50g Belazu green [[tapenade]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the cauliflowers into florets and chop the remaining stalk into 0.5cm [[Dice|dice]]. Peel and finely chop the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]].\n| Melt the [[Butter|butter]] in a large pan, add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Thyme|thyme]] sprigs and cook over a low heat until softened but not coloured.\n| Add the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] florets and [[Stock|stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15-20 minutes until the florets are tender.\n| Remove from the heat and leave to cool.\n| Bring a small pan of [[Salted|salted]] water to the [[Boil|boil]], add the chopped [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] stalk and cook for a minute or two until tender. Drain and refresh with cold water. Drain again and set aside.\n| Coarsely grate the [[gruy\u00e8re]] and chop the [[Parsley|parsley]].\n| Pick out the [[Thyme|thyme]] and blend the [[Soup|soup]] in batches until very smooth.\n| Season well and pour back into the pan. Reheat with the [[Cream|cream]] or mile, adding the [[Blanched|blanched]] [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] stalk and [[Parsley|parsley]] at the end and check the seasoning.\n| Ladle the [[Soup|soup]] into bowls, stir a spoonful of [[tapenade]] into each and scatter with a little [[Grated|grated]] [[gruy\u00e8re]].\n}}\n(''Annie Nichols in The Sunday Telegraph-Stella''))\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/green-tapenade.html Belazu Green Tapenade]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cauliflower #thyme #garlic #onion #parsley #boil #soup #cream #butter #tapenade #cauliflowersoupwithgreentapenade </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe is also quick and easy to prepare and very easy to adapt so it suits your personal taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 large [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]], plus extra for drizzling\n| 150g (5oz) [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]], [[defrosted]]\n| 1 large [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Cheese, garlic and chili mayonnaise]] or [[almogrote]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sherry|sherry]] or [[White wine|white wine]]\n| [[Sea salt]] and freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 1 wholemeal bread roll, blitzed to breadcrumbs in a [[blender]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Slice off the tops, leaving the stem intact; reserve.\n| With deft knife-work, remove the white membranes and knock out the [[Seeds|seeds]].\n| Heat the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and flavour it with a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] for 4 minutes, add the [[Peas|peas]] and saut\u00e9 for a further 4 minutes.\n| Remove from the heat.\n| Add the breadcrumbs and cheese mayonnaise and mix really well.\n| Add a twist of [[black pepper]] and a sprinkle of [[salt]] to each of the sweet peppers\n| Distribute the [[Pea|pea]] mixture between the [[Peppers|peppers]].\n| Drizzle with a little more [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and the [[sherry]].\n| Replace the tops, place in an oven dish, cover with [[tin-foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 35 minutes or until cooked to your liking.\n}}\n==See also==\n* [[Pea and garlic stuffed peppers]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#blackpepper #oliveoil #sherry #unusualrecipes #miseenplace #onions #whitewine #frozenpeas #defrosted #peas #redonion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I love to add [[Cream cheese|cream cheese]] and [[Mustard|mustard]]; what's your favourite?\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 roll ready made [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]]\n| 3 tablespoon [[Philadelphia Russell's of Upwell's]]\n| 100g gruy\u00e8re [[Cheese|cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 beaten [[Egg|egg]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] into [[Philadelphia cream cheese]] ensuring the mixture is well combined\n| Add a dollop of mustardy [[Cream cheese|cream cheese]] into the centre of each square of [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]]\n| Lay a rasher of [[Bacon|bacon]] diagonally over each mound of [[Cream cheese|cream cheese]]\n| Scatter the [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]] over the [[Bacon|bacon]]\n| Although considered wisdom suggests using egg wash to join the pastry, my experiments show it's better to twist the dry pastry edges together to join them\n| Fold all four bare corners of the [[Pastry|pastry]] together and press together to seal\n| [[Brush]] the tops of the [[Pastry|pastry]] with the beaten [[Egg|egg]]\n| Slide the [[Pastries|pastries]] onto a greaseproof backing sheet or [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 20 '''''or''''' until golden [[Brown|brown]]\n| Move to as [[Cooling rack|cooling rack]] to cool, once [[Baked|baked]]\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nThese keep perfectly well for 4 days if [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French title": "Cheese and bacon quiche",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cheese and bacon quiche\n|titlemode=replace\n|description=With lovely Fresh fresh eggs from Thelma and Louise, making quiches is a must.\n|keywords=#pastry #greaseproofpaper #dehydrated #brie #eggs #freshlygroundblackpepper #parsley #bacon #cheddarcheese #bake #oliveoil #quiche\n|hashtagrev=12032020\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=3rd July 2022\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  4 hours, 20 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 10 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 3007\n|PortionCalories = 751\n|Image = [[Image:Cheese and bacon quiche recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very continental</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Especially like the sun-dried tomatoes</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Cheese and bacon quiche baked.jpg|thumb|right|Baked in a Le Cruset oven dish]]\n\nWith lovely [[Fresh eggs|fresh eggs]] from [[Thelma and Louise]], [[Thelma and Louise|(our hens)]] making quiches is a must.  This one used bits and bobs we had lying about; it was fabulous.  Very juicy, which I think must have been the re-hydrated [[Taste Sensation Sun-dried Tomatoes Diced]] coupled with the fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n\nNormally, using a metal flan tin a percentage of the pasty is always left-over and wasted, this time I used the cast [[Iron|iron]] [[Le Creuset]]  rectangular [[Oven|oven]] dish.  The [[Pastry|pastry]] fitted perfectly, with no wastage.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 pack [[Ready rolled shortcrust pastry|ready rolled shortcrust pastry]]\n| 5 large [[Eggs|eggs]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[cr\u00e8me fra\u00eeche]]\n| Pinch of [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| A big pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 5 rashers of [[Bacon|bacon]], chopped into small pieces\n| 2 [[Cloves of garlic, crushed|cloves of garlic, crushed]]\n| 150 g [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| 50 g [[French]] [[Brie|brie]], chopped into small cubes\n| 3 tablespoons [[Taste Sensation Sun-dried Tomatoes Diced]]\n| 10 [[Cherry tomatoes|cherry tomatoes]], sliced\n| Good pinch of sweet [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Soak the [[Dehydrated|dehydrated]] [[Sun-dried tomatoes|sun-dried tomatoes]] in water for 3 hours\n* Drain in a [[Sieve|sieve]] before use.\n* Pre-heat you [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove the pre-rolled [[Pastry|pastry]] from the [[Fridge|fridge]] and leave at room temperature for an hour to allow easy handling\n| Roll the [[Pastry|pastry]] into the [[Oven tray|oven tray]]\n| Cover with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]]\n| Fill the paper with [[Baking beans|baking beans]] and [[Blind bake|blind bake]] for 15 minutes at 180\u00b0 C \n| Remove the [[Beans|beans]] and [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]] and prick the [[Pastry|pastry]] all over with a fork\n| Return to the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 7 minutes to crisp up\n| Meanwhile [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 5 minutes in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]], adding the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] for the last few minutes\n| [[Stir fry]] the [[Bacon|bacon]] in this mixture until it is slightly [[Browned|browned]] and all of the  moisture is bubbled off from the bacon\n| [[Whisk]] the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[cr\u00e8me fra\u00eeche]] and [[Parsley|parsley]] together until smooth\n| Remove the [[Pastry|pastry]] from the [[Oven|oven]] and allow to cool for 10 minutes\n| Dot the [[Brie|brie]] evenly over the [[Pastry|pastry]] base\n| Pour in the [[Egg|egg]] mixture and evenly distribute the remaining main ingredients evenly over the mix, topping with half of the [[Cheddar cheese]] and a sprinkle of [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| [[Bake]] for 40 minutes at  160\u00b0 C - checking after 30 to ensure the [[Pastry|pastry]] does not burn\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Chef's notes===\nThe long preparation time is due to the time it takes to rehydrate the [[Sun-dried tomatoes|sun-dried tomatoes]].  Obviously with jarred sun-[[Dried|dried]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] this step would not be necessary!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#pastry #greaseproofpaper #dehydrated #brie #eggs #freshlygroundblackpepper #parsley #bacon #cheddarcheese #bake #oliveoil #quiche</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cheese and potato croquettes a cheese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#potatoes #breadcrumbs #cheeseandpotatocroquettes #cheese #egg #springonions #baking #sesameseeds #bake #chilipowder #flour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=If what I'm hearing is true and you can't find these in the shops anymore, make your own, it's simple. Go posh and try with more exotic cheeses such as\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2135\n|PortionCalories = 533\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Cheese and potato croquettes, ready to bake or freeze\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 10 minutes\n|PrepTime = 35 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Garlic and cornmeal potato nuggets to freeze.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Yummy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I hadn't thought of freezing them - neat idea and tasty.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nIf what I'm hearing is true and you can't find these in the shops anymore, make your own, it's simple.\n\nGo posh and try with more exotic [[cheeses]] such as Camembert or Roquefort.  With a sort [[cheese]] that won't grate easily, you may be better to mould potato mixture around the cheese rather than mix in with the [[potatoes]].\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 large [[baking]] [[potatoes]] (Desiree, Estima, Marfona or Vivaldi) if you can get them\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[Emmental]] or [[Cheddar cheese]], [[grated]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[butter]] or [[olive oil]]\n| 2 [[spring onions]], [[chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 [[egg]], beaten\n|  50 g (2 oz) [[plain flour]]\n| Bunch of [[parsley leaves]], chopped\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Pinch if [[chili powder]] (optional)\n| 2 tablespoons [[sesame seeds]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) fresh [[breadcrumbs]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Bake]] the [[potatoes]] at 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4) for 1 hour or until cooked; allow to cool so they can be handled. Peel and [[mash]] with a [[potato masher]] or [[potato ricer]].\n| In a bowl, combine the [[cheese]], [[spring onions]], one of the [[eggs]], [[parsley]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]], [[chili powder]] if using, and [[potatoes]].\n| Squish up the mixture with your (clean) hands so it's well combined.\n| Pour the [[breadcrumbs]] onto a plate and mix in the [[sesame seeds]].\n| Mould the croquettes into shape, a bit bigger than golf-balls, then roll into sausage shapes\n| Dredge these in the [[flour]], then in the beaten [[egg]] mixture, then roll then in the [[breadcrumbs]]\n| Refrigerate for 30 minutes to set\n| Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4)\n| Place the croquettes on a non-stick [[baking]] tray and [[bake]] for 35 minutes or until golden brown.\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\n\nThe next time you cook [[jacket potatoes]], add a few extra and save them for making this dish.  They'll keep in the [[fridge]] for a few days.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Garlic and cornmeal potato nuggets]]\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croquette\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potatoes #breadcrumbs #cheeseandpotatocroquettes #cheese #egg #springonions #baking #sesameseeds #bake #chilipowder #flour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Dried|dried]] dill will do at a push\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Juice]] from half a [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n}}\n====for the sauce====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200 ml [[Double Cream|double cream]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Dijon Mustard|dijon mustard]]\n| The [[Zest|zest]] from half a [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| A tablespoon of [[Capers|capers]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Lay out your sheets of [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]] (or roll it out)\n| Pop the [[Fish|fish]] slices into a bowl, sprinkle with [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Allow to [[Marinate|marinate]] for 30 minutes.\n| Sprinkle the insides of the [[Puff pastry|puff pastry]] with [[Panko]] [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and lay the [[Fish|fish]] fillets on top.\n| Coat with [[Mustard|mustard]] and then sprinkle with [[Grated|grated]] [[:Category:D\u017eiugas cheese recipes|D\u017eiugas cheese]].\n| Fold the [[Pastry|pastry]] up and pinch the edges to make a good seal.\n| Cut a slot in the top of the [[Pastry|pastry]] so [[Steam|steam]] can escape.\n| [[Brush]] with the beaten [[Egg|egg]].\n| [[Bake]] on a non-stick [[Baking tray|baking tray]] at 200\u00b0 C for 15 minutes then reduce the heat to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 140\u00b0 C] and bake for a further 15 minutes or until nicely [[Browned|browned]].\n}}\n====sauce====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Cream|cream]] to a small pan together with the [[Zest|zest]] from half a [[Lemon|lemon]], season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and gently [[Simmer|simmer]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the [[Fish|fish]] pasties with the creamy [[Sauce|sauce]] and sprinkle with [[Capers|capers]].\n===Variations===\nFor a nice change (and an economical one) try using [[Basa fillets|basa fillets]] instead of [[Cod|cod]].\n\nIf you can't get [[D\u017eiugas cheese]], try Parmesan cheese, it's quite similar.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:D\u017eiugas cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#puffpastry #fish #lemon #cheesycodbitesinpuffpastryparcels #dijonmustard #zest #grated #panko #pastry #cod #breadcrumbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken Marengo, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #tomatoes #oliveoil #eggs #garlic #onions #chickenmarengo #crayfish #basilleaves #simmer #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Chicken Marengo is an Italian savoury dish, so named for being the dish that Napoleon Bonaparte ate after the Battle of Marengo. According to tradition\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2849\n|PortionCalories = 712\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|ImageComment = Napoleon statue at Cherbourg\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 20 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Napoleon Marengo.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I make something like this often...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">...using left-overs.  I just never knew this was what it was called!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''[[Chicken]] Marengo''' is an Italian savoury dish, so named for being the dish that Napol\u00e9on Bonaparte ate after the Battle of Marengo.\n\nAccording to tradition Napoleon demanded a quick meal after the battle and his chef was forced to work with the meagre results of a forage: a [[chicken]] (and some [[eggs]]), [[tomatoes]], [[onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[herbs]], [[olive oil]], and [[crayfish]]. The chef cut up the chicken (reportedly with a sabre) and [[fried]] it in [[olive oil]], made a [[sauce]] from the [[tomatoes]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[onions]] (plus a bit of cognac from Napoleon's flask), cooked the crayfish, fried the [[eggs]] and served them as a garnish, with some of the soldier's [[bread]] ration on the side. Napoleon reportedly liked the dish and (having won the battle) considered it lucky. He refused to have the ingredients altered on future occasions even when his chef tried to omit the crayfish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[crayfish]] tails\n| 1.2kg whole [[chicken]], jointed\n| 1 large [[onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 [[clove]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], crushed\n| 6 [[tomatoes]], chopped or 1 small can of [[tomatoes]], chopped\n| 6 tablespoons [[brandy]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[plain flour]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n| Handful of torn [[basil leaves]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[black olives]]\n| 2 Free range [[eggs]] to garnish -(optional but authentic!) \n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]]\n| [[Joint the chicken]]\n| Season the [[flour]] with [[salt]] and [[pepper]] and roll the [[chicken]] pieces in the [[flour]] \n| In a large pot, heat the [[olive oil]] and brown the [[chicken]] pieces, reserve and keep warm\n| Add the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] (and a little more [[olive oil]] if needed) and soften the [[onions]]\n| Add the [[chicken]] back to the pan and add the [[tomatoes]] and [[brandy]], cover and [[simmer]] on a low heat for 30 minutes\n| Add the [[crayfish]] tails and [[simmer]] for a further 10 minutes\n| At the last minutes, stir in the [[basil leaves]] and [[olives]]\n| [[Fry]] the [[eggs]] and serve as a garnish with the finished dish\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nTo win all of your battles, serve with crusty [[bread]] or [[boiled potatoes]]\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #tomatoes #oliveoil #eggs #garlic #onions #chickenmarengo #crayfish #basilleaves #simmer #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

However, not everyone has a [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]], so the next best thing is to [[Steam|steam]] them.  It will take twice as long but the results will be the same.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Globe artichokes|globe artichokes]]\n| A selection of [[Dips|dips]] to serve, eg:\n| ''[[garlic mayonnaise]]''\n| ''[[Lemon butter for fish|lemon butter]]''\n| ''[[Balsamic vinegar and olive oil dip]]''\n| ''[[Sour cream and chive dip]]''\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cooking globe artichokes in a pressure cooker recipe.jpg|Remove the hairy centre and you're down to the heart of the choke\nImage:Trim a third of the choke and discard.jpg|Trim a third of the choke and discard\nImage:Globe artichokes peeled.jpg|Peel the stem and trim to 2.5 cm\nImage:Two globe artichokes ready to prepare.jpg|Globe artichokes ready to prepare\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Some suggest trimming the spike from each 'leaf' or 'petal', however, on mine there is not much of a spike and that feels rather unnecessary as there is no culinary benefit in doing this\n| Using a [[Speed peeler|speed peeler]], remove the skin from the stem as it can make the choke [[Bitter|bitter]]\n| Trim the stem to about 2.5 cm (1 \")\n| Remove the top third of the [[Artichoke|artichoke]] and discard\n| Add a squeeze of [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] over the cut area\n| Fill the [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]] to just under the trivet with [[Boiling|boiling]] water\n| Smash a [[Clove|clove]] of unpeeled [[Garlic|garlic]] under the flat of a knife and add to the water\n| If you have the squeezed [[Lemons|lemons]] add these together with the [[Artichokes|artichokes]] to the [[Steamer|steamer]] basket and sit on the trivet\n| Cook for 7 minutes on high pressure and let the [[Cooker|cooker]] depressurise naturally\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe warm or cold with a selection of [[dips]].\n\nYou'll need a large bowl for all of the discarded nibbles.\n\nPull each 'leaf' out, dip and pare the buttery part of the leaf with your teeth and then discard it.\n\nWhen you have nibbled all of the leaves, remove the hairy centre and you are at the heart of the choke. You can scoop this out with a spoon or quarter the 'cup', dip and nibble the quarters.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pressurecooker #cookingglobeartichokesinapressurecooker #dips #globeartichokes #garlicmayonnaise #steamer #artichoke #bitter #boiling #unusualrecipes #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

#bayleaf \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=..and back into the 70's we go\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1708\n|PortionCalories = 284\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 4 hours 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 20 minutes\n|CookTime = 4 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Coq au vin (3/4 pint) good [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 150 ml (1/4 pint) water\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 1 sprig freshly picked [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| 2 tablespoons freshly chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3) \n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse and dry the [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| [[Joint the chicken]] into 6 or eight pieces\n| Melt 25 g ( 1 oz) of the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan or [[Wok|wok]] with the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the lardons until [[Browned|browned]]\n| Place the lardons in a 3 pint ovenproof casserole dish\n| In the [[Wok|wok]], [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces until [[Brown|brown]] and sealed, add to the casserole dish\n| To peel the [[Shallots|shallots]], soak for 20 seconds in [[Boiling|boiling]] water, then plunge into cold water.\n| Gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Shallots|shallots]] and [[Celery|celery]] for 5 minutes then add to the casserole dish\n| Melt the remaining [[Butter|butter]] in the [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] for 3 minutes, set aside\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] to the [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 30 seconds, then stir in the seasoned [[Flour|flour]] until the [[Fat|fat]] is absorbed\n| Add the [[Wine|wine]], water [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste and [[Simmer|simmer]] until it thickens a little\n| Pour the [[Wine|wine]] mixture over the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces\n| Cover with a lid or [[tin foil]] and cook for 3 hours, 45 minutes\n| Drain any surface [[Fat|fat]] with kitchen paper\n| Remove the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and any woody [[Thyme|thyme]], stir in the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]], cover and return to the oven for 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with plain [[Boiled potatoes|boiled potatoes]] and [[Carrots|carrots]].\n\n===Variations===\n\nFor a nice change, try serving this with [[Pasta|pasta]].\n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:French title": "Court bouillon",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Court bouillon, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#courtbouillon #whitewine #lemon #fishandseafood #boil #simmer #sieve #garlic #bouquetgarni #frozen #blackpepper \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Court-bouillon or court bouillon is a flavoured liquid for poaching or quick-cooking foods\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 262\n|PortionCalories = 43\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Servings: 6 - Makes about 1 litre (pan size dependent)\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Court bouillon.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Great for poaching basa</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">My favourite stock for cooking basa, my favourite fish.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Court-bouillon''' or '''court bouillon''' is a flavoured liquid for [[poaching]] or quick-cooking foods. Nowadays, it is usually mentioned in connection with [[fish and seafood]], but it is also used for poaching [[vegetables]], [[eggs]], and delicate [[meats]] such as cockscombs, sweetbreads, and the like.\n\nCourt-bouillon is 'short' (the literal meaning of the French word 'court') because the cooking time is brief in comparison with a rich and complex [[stock]], and generally is not served as part of the finished dish. Since delicate foods do not cook for very long, it is prepared before the foods are added.\n\nFor [[fish]], it is generally a mixture of water, acid ([[white wine]] or [[lemon]]), [[salt]], [[bouquet garni]], and [[black pepper]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 [[leek]], chopped\n| 1 [[onion]], chopped\n| 1 [[carrot]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 [[celery]] stick, chopped\n| 1 [[clove]] [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| 1 sprig [[thyme]]\n| Few [[parsley]] stalks\n| 1 sprig [[tarragon]]\n| Handful of [[basil leaves]]\n| &#189; [[lemon]], sliced\n| 1 [[star anise]]\n| 100ml [[white wine]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all the ingredients in a large pan\n| Cover with cold water and bring to the [[boil]]. [[Simmer]] gently for 30 minutes, then strain through a [[muslin]]-lined [[sieve]]\n| Will keep for 5 days if refrigerated or 3 months if [[frozen]]\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#courtbouillon #whitewine #lemon #fishandseafood #boil #simmer #sieve #garlic #bouquetgarni #frozen #blackpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Ideally from un-sliced white bread, though brown bread makes an interesting change\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 586\n|PortionCalories = 146\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 minutes\n |CookTime = 8 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Croutons recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I'll never buy ready made again.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">These re so simple to make. A no-brainer - make your own! </span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nA simple [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to [[Soups|soups]] and [[Salads|salads]].  Ideally from un-sliced [[White bread|white bread]], though [[Brown bread|brown bread]] makes an interesting change.  They are probably better made with stale [[Bread|bread]].\n\nThey can be made in an [[Oven|oven]], but I find a heavy based [[Frying|frying]]-pan to be just as good, and a little quicker.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| About 175 g (6 oz) of stale [[Bread|bread]] - crusts removed\n| 2 to 3 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Butter|butter]]\n| Fine [[Table salt|table salt]]\n| 1 clove of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]] (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove the crusts and cut the [[Bread|bread]] into cubes\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Butter|butter]] in the pan until frothing\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] if using and [[Fry|fry]] for 25 seconds\n| Toss in the [[Croutons|croutons]] and jiggle the pan so the [[Oil|oil]] is evenly distributed and [[Fry|fry]] until golden [[Brown|brown]]\n| Sprinkle with a little [[Salt|salt]] and serve.\n| They will keep if stored in an airtight container, but they are so quick and simple to make it's probably easier to make them as you need them.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf , like me you prefer you [[Croutons|croutons]] drier, just use half the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Butter|butter]].  They are just as nice.\n\nShould you want to cook them in the oven, preheat to 180\u00b0C (gas mark 4 / 350\u00b0F), using a bowl, toss them in just oil, spread out on a baking sheet and bake for about 10 minutes.  They could also be done under a grill, but watch them closely or they will burn!\n===Chef's notes===\nAs a rough guide, 1 bread roll makes enough croutons for 2 people; [[ciabatta]] rolls make really nice croutons.\n\n{{Template:Croutons recipes}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#croutonsrecipe #bread #butter #fry #garlic #croutons #tablesalt #soups #brownbread #whitebread #ciabatta </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Don't allow the garlic to burn or it will be horrid and [[Bitter|bitter]].\n| Allow the [[Garlic|garlic]] to cool then pour into a bowl and whisk in the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| Add the [[Yoghurt|yoghurt]] and mix really well.\n| [[Refrigerate]] and allow the flavours to amalgamate if time allows.\n| Mix the [[Salad|salad]] in with the [[Yoghurt|yoghurt]] so it resembles a [[Cole-slaw|cole-slaw]] and serve.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Crunchy garlic salad the basic ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The basic ingredients\nImage:Crunchy garlic salad the pre mix.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to mix in the garlic oil\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe dressed with chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] and sliced [[Onion|onion]] rings.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nThis delicious [[salad]] lasted the pair of us two days in the end.  Make up the [[yogurt]] dressing in one go, use half the [[salad]] and refrigerate the remaining salad and mix them together when you want to use it.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#salad #garlic #crunchygarlicsalad #yoghurt #parsley #oliveoil #lemonjuice #bitter #crunchysalad #frying #fat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

minutes per side.\n| Set to one side and keep warm.\n| Lower the heat and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] until softened, about 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Tuna|tuna]] and                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Dauphinois potatoes a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dauphinoispotatoes #potatoes #oliveoil #nutmeg #butter #potato #grated #philadelphiadauphinoisepotatoes #cheese #doublecream #scallopedpotatoesrecipe \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Luxurious, extravagant and rich, this dish, that originates from Dauphine in the French Alps, is simple and easy to cook\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1687\n|PortionCalories = 421\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours\n|PrepTime = 30 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Dauphinois potatoes.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Grannies potato dish.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Really tasty as I love the crunchy bits, but this always feels old fashioned and reminds me of me gran!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>}}\n[[Image:Dauphinois potatoes recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Dauphinois potatoes ready for the oven]]\nLuxurious, extravagant and rich, this dish, that originates from Dauphine in the French Alps, is simple and easy to cook.  Just mind you don't have it everyday!\n\nWhilst not authentic, any opportunity to use [[Gruy\u00e8re cheese]] has to be taken up!\n\nThis recipe is similar to [[Scalloped potatoes recipe|Scalloped potatoes]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[potatoes]], Cara, King Edward or Desiree\n| 1 [[clove garlic, crushed]]\n| 142 ml (5 fl oz) [[milk]]  \n| 142 ml (5 fl oz) [[double cream]]\n| Freshly [[grated]] [[nutmeg]]\n| 25 g ( 1 oz) [[butter]]\n| Dash of [[olive oil]]\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[Gruy\u00e8re cheese]], [[grated]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Preheat the oven to 150\u00b0 C (300\u00b0 F - Gas 2)\n| Peel the [[potatoes]] and slice thinly with a [[food processor]] or a [[mandoline]]\n| Rinse the sliced [[potatoes]] in cold water to remove excess starch\n| Dry them with a tea-towel\n| Rub a gratin dish with the [[olive oil]]\n| Building up in layers, add; [[potato]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] until all the [[potato]] is used\n| Mix the [[milk]], [[cream]] and [[cheese]] together and grate a little [[nutmeg]] into the mixture.\n| Pour over the layered [[potatoes]]\n| Top with dabs of [[butter]] and [[bake]] on the top shelf of the oven for an hour and a half\n}}\n==See also ==\n* [[Philadelphia dauphinoise potatoes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dauphinoispotatoes #potatoes #oliveoil #nutmeg #butter #potato #grated #philadelphiadauphinoisepotatoes #cheese #doublecream #scallopedpotatoesrecipe </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Duck, leek and chorizo cassoulet",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Duck, leek and chorizo cassoulet\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onions #slowcooker #fat #russellsofupwellduck #duck #duckfat #bacon #chorizo #sherryvinegar #budweiser\n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Another variation of this French classic using produce from Russell's' Butchers of Upwell.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=21st December 2022\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 hours\n|TotalCalories = 1720\n|PortionCalories = 860\n|Image = [[Image:Duck, leek and chorizo cassoulet.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very nice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Almost like you get in Bordeaux!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Duck, leek and chorizo cassoulet slow cooked.jpg|thumb|right|After 1 hour in the slow cooker - \ud83d\ude0b]]\nMy own variation on this French classic.  A very economical meal, one duck leg, half a chorizo sausage and one large leek and butter beans are the basics for this recipe.\n\nThis recipe is cooked in the [[Slow-cooker|slow-cooker]]; just starting off in a cast [[Iron|iron]] [[Frying pan|frying pan]] to [[Brown|brown]] the [[Duck|duck]], [[chorizo]] and [[leeks]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 large [[Duck|duck]] leg, skin on, from Russell's of Upwell if you're lucky enough to live in Norfolk!\n| Half a link of chorizo sausage.\n| 3 rashers of Russel's treacly [[Bacon|bacon]] - (fatty back bacon [[Cured|cured]] in [[Black treacle|black treacle]])\n| 1 large [[leek]], washed and chopped into rings\n| 3 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 3 [[Thin Indian green chillies|thin indian green chillies]], left whole\n| 1 400g can of chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 400g can of [[Butter beans|butter beans]]\n| 1 bottle of [[Budweiser]] beer (300 ml)\n| 1 crumbled chicken stock cube\n| Big pinch of [[Taste Sensation Italian seasoning]]\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove the skin from the chorizo by peeling it off\n| Chop the chorizo into rings\n| Using no [[Fat|fat]] at all, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Duck|duck]] leg for 10 minutes in a heavy based pan to [[Brown|brown]] and release the [[Duck fat|duck fat]] from the skin\n| Chop the [[Bacon|bacon]] rashers into bite-sized pieces and [[Fry|fry]] them together with the [[chorizo slices]] for 3 or 4 minutes to colour them\n| Leaving the [[Fat|fat]] in the pan, remove all the [[Meat|meat]] and place in the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] while you cook the [[leeks]]\n| [[Sautee]] the [[leeks]] for 5 minutes until until well [[Browned|browned]]\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minute or so\n| Tip the contents of the pan into the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] and [[Deglaze|deglaze]] the pan with the [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| Mix all of the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], drained [[Beans|beans]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and seasoning together and stir well to combine\n| Add all of this to the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] together with the [[Budwesier]] mixed with the stock cube and slow cook on high for 2 hours\n| After 2 hours, stir well, remove and discard the whole [[Chillies|chillies]], turn the [[Slow-cooker|slow-cooker]] down to low and cook for the remaining two hours.\n| Remove the duck leg from the slow cooker, shred the meat from the leg and serve directly onto the plates and pour over the beans and sausage mixture.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with plain boiled potatoes\n===Recipe source===\n* Based on an idea bought to me by produce sold by the [[Butchers|butchers]] I can see from here!\n===Chef's notes===\nAlmost anything you love can be added to this, the [[Duck fat|duck fat]] and the [[Beans|beans]] are the mainstay of this recipe to my mind, but anything you have top [[Hand|hand]] will be fabulous in this hearty [[Soup|soup]]-cum-[[Stew|stew]] recipe\n==See also==\n* [https://www.facebook.com/people/Russells-Family-Butchers/100063462076744/?paipv=0&eav=AfY1bdaLsrKyd7lZwxlS3oVF2YMWaPhrzCHWXKcQ3R8QqU018A93uyL5jG6NTEpPsC8&_rdr Russell's of Upwell (Facebook page)]\n* [[Cassoulet|Other good cassoulet recipes]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork title": "Duck and sausage cassoulet",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Duck and sausage cassoulet, French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#duckandsausagecassoulet #pancetta #thyme #whitewine #driedchillies #lardons #sherry #kilner #plumtomatoes #unusualrecipes #redwine \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I'm no great fan of modern-day TV cookery programs. Jamie and Hugh are great but after that you need to go back to Floyd and Fanny to keep me happy\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5234\n|PortionCalories = 872\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet, bread added and crisped\n |Servings = 6 to 8 people\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 35 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">An odd combination</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Quite a strange mixture; duck and sausages, but it works admirably.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI'm no great fan of modern-day TV [[Cookery|cookery]] programs. Jamie and Hugh are great but after that you need to go back to Floyd and Fanny to keep me happy.  However, things changed last week when I  saw the Fabulous Baker Brothers [Channel 4 UK].  Fresh lively presentation with relatively complex food, simply explained and cooked. I am a convert.  \n\nCassoulet is typical of [[Aquitaine]], South West [[France]], though can probably be found throughout Southern France.  In French shops and markets you would find the [[Beans|beans]] in [[Kilner]]-type jars, sealed with a layer of [[Duck fat|duck fat]] rather than being sold in tins.\n\nI have adjusted the quantities, cooking temperatures and times from both the tv program and the Channel 4 recipe, see [[Talk:Duck and sausage cassoulet| the comments page]] for my reasons.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 6 [[Toulouse sausages]] (about 400g)\n| 4 [[Duck|duck]] legs\n| 6 rashers of [[Pancetta|pancetta]]\n| 2 x 400g cans of peeled [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 1 bulb of [[Garlic|garlic]], unpeeled and cut in two\n|* ''When I cut my bulb in two, a lot of the outer skin came away so I actually removed most of it.''\n| 2 medium [[Red onions|red onions]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 large [[Red chilli|red chilli]], slit lengthwise\n| 3 sprigs of [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 500 ml [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| A good splash of [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 2 x 400g cans [[Cannellini beans|cannellini beans]], well rinsed in cold water and drained\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 1 [[French baguette]], torn into small pieces\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet pre bread.jpg|The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet, ready for the bread\nImage:The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet tight fit.jpg|This is the largest roasting tray I have and I could only get 400 ml of stock in it!\nImage:The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet fryin tray.jpg|Use the roasting tray like a huge frying pan\nImage:The Fabulous Baker Brothers cassoulet ingredients.jpg|The ingredients\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Pour a splash of olive oil into a large roasting pan on a hob at a high heat.  Add a grind of [[black pepper]], add the duck and sausages and use it like a huge frying pan to brown the meat.  This may take 10 to 15 minutes.\n| Remove the browned meat and set to one side.\n|Slit the chilli length-wise but don't disturb the seeds.\n| With the heat still on, add the herbs, chilli, onions, pancetta, garlic bulb halves, cut side down.  Season with salt and pepper and fry for 5 minutes, stirring now and then.\n| [[De-glaze]] the pan with the wine and the sherry vinegar.\n| Add the beans and chopped tomatoes and mix well.\n| Arrange the duck and sausages on the top, duck skin-side up.  Pour over the chicken stock and jiggle the roasting tray to bed everything down.\n| Roast uncovered for 1.5 hours, checking a few times to see that it's not drying out. ''see [[Talk:Duck and sausage cassoulet|comments]]''\n| After 1.5 hours, tear the baguette into small pieces and push into the tray so that the bread soaks up all the fat and juices.\n| Return to the oven and roast for 30 minutes more.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nOn the TV program they suggested serving with a green salad. I'm not sure that would work very well. We found it fine on its own, though it might be nice with some boiled broccoli.\n===Variations===\n* Instead of [[pancetta]], use 200 g [[dry cured bacon]] or [[lardons]]\n* Use dry [[Sherry|sherry]] or even [[red wine]] instead of [[white wine]]\n* Use 1 cup (450g / 1lb) dried cannellini beans though they will need soaking overnight, rinsing and boiling in unsalted water for 1 to 1.5 hours before they can be added at the same stage as the canned beans.\n* I added a few ''interesting'' [[dried chillies]] instead of the large fresh red chilli.\n* My fresh thyme is a little past its best so I made a [[bouquet garni]] of some [[thyme]], [[bay leaves]] and a little [[cutting celery]]\n==See also==\n* [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:English_television_chefs Television chefs (Wikipedia)]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#duckandsausagecassoulet #pancetta #thyme #whitewine #driedchillies #lardons #sherry #kilner #plumtomatoes #unusualrecipes #redwine </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Easy sausage and bean cassoulet",

We had a small ciabatta loaf, pack of Toulouse sausages\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 6613\n|PortionCalories = 1653\n|DatePublished=12th January 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = OK, it might look like cat sick but it was glorious!\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  55 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Easy sausage and bean cassoulet recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Much better than it looks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Tasted fabulous, looks rubbish!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]])</span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Mogettes a la paysan.jpg|300px|thumb|right|One of the many variants of bottled white French beans]]\nUse this recipe as a starting point for your imagination!\n\nWe had a small [[Ciabatta|ciabatta]] loaf, pack of [[Toulouse sausages]] from [[Gourmet sausage maker - Bexley]] and a large bottle of [[French]] [[Flageolet beans|flageolet beans]] from our summer holiday.  The [[Rest|rest]] of the ingredients were  odds and ends.\n\nI find the [[French]] bottled [[mogettes]] \u00e0 la paysanne to be a little cloying so I tried to adjust this with the [[Creme fraiche|creme fraiche]].  Serving with the [[Steamed broccoli|steamed broccoli]] was almost like a palate cleaner. The result was excellent and will be made again.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| A good pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 6 [[Toulouse sausages]], cut in half\n| 850 ml jar of [[mogettes \u00e0 la paysanne]] - not sure if you would find these in the UK but they are very common in mid-France\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] or [[Tex-Mex seasoning]]\n| 2 tablespoons of ruby [[Port|port]]\n| 5 tablespoons of [[Creme fraiche|creme fraiche]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to a [[Dutch Oven|dutch oven]], when hot add the chopped [[Onions|onions]] and the halved [[Toulouse sausages]] and [[Saute|saute]] for 4 minutes\n| Stir in the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and [[Saute|saute]] for a minute or so\n| Tip in the mogettes and the [[Taco seasoning]] and [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] and mix well\n| Bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]], reduce the heat to very low and simmer for about 40 minutes. As you can get quite a lot of [[Steam|steam]] from this you can adjust the consistency to your liking by [[Simmering|simmering]] covered or with the lid half on.\n| When there is about 5 minutes left to go, begin [[Steaming|steaming]] the [[Broccoli|broccoli]].\n| Stir in the [[Port|port]] and [[Creme fraiche|creme fraiche]] and mix well.  Bring back to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and remove from the heat. Ensure the mixture does not [[Boil|boil]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Steamed broccoli|steamed broccoli]] and sliced [[Ciabatta bread|ciabatta bread]]\n===Variations===\nOdd [[Vegetables|vegetables]] can be mixed in too.  I found a spare [[Tomato|tomato]] chopped it up and added it to the mix\n\n===See also ===\n* [[Cassoulet recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#toulousesausages #cremefraiche #steamedbroccoli #tomatopuree #blackpepper #easysausageandbeancassoulet #french #simmer #port #oliveoil #saute </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Fish baked in sea salt",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sea bass fish baked in sea salt, French recipe Hugh Fearnley-Whittingstall\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #fishbakedinseasalt #seabass #bream #dill #sauce #fennel #lemon #parsley #france #bakingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I first cooked this dish in a camper van, on a beach in Vieux Boucau, Aquitaine, France, many years ago\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 556\n|PortionCalories = 278\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Not a grain of salt on the fish\n |Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Fish baked in sea salt recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not a taste of salt</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Strange idea which works, and it really is not salty.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nI first cooked this dish in a camper van, on a beach in Vieux Boucau, [[Aquitaine]], [[France]], many years ago.  The [[Salt|salt]] seems to make it easy to remove the skin and keeps the [[Fish|fish]] really moist - it's also quite an impressive looking dish. We bought most of the ingredients from the local fishmonger who strangely, looked exactly like Poseidon himself!\n\nDon't be worried about the amount of [[Salt|salt]] used, it sticks to (and helps to remove) the skin and does not make the dish the least bit salty. The large [[Grains|grains]] of coarse [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] don't seem to permeate the [[Fish|fish]]. In [[France]], [[Sel gris]], the grey coloured [[Sea salt|sea salt]] is cheap and easily available in all supermarkets, that won't be the case in the UK unfortunately.\n  \nYou really do need coarse [[sea salt]] for this recipe, and quite a lot.  I've heard of 'the careful' using dishwasher salt for this though I would read the packaging very carefully first!\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Lemon and parsley sauce.jpg|[[Lemon and parsley sauce]], simple, quick and effective\nImage:Fish in salt, baked.jpg|[[Baked|baked]] after 25 minutes\nImage:Two bream baked in sea salt recipe.jpg|Layer two, the second [[bream]] added. This works better with just one large fish.\n</gallery>\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 Whole [[white fish]]; [[Sea bass|sea bass]]; sea [[Bream|bream]], etc.\n| Bunch of fresh [[Dill|dill]] or [[Fennel]]\n| Bunch of fresh [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| &#188; of an [[Onion|onion]], roughly sliced\n| Very coarse [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to cover\n|* Don't try to use fine-grained [[table salt]]\n}}\n'''Parsley and lemon sauce'''\n* 50g (2 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n* 1 whole [[Lemon|lemon]]\n* 1 bunch [[parsley]] leaves, finely chopped\n* Seasoning \n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0C; 350\u00b0 F; gas Mk 4; Moderate/Medium\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Dry the [[Fish|fish]] skin with a [[Paper towel|paper towel]] and stuff the belly cavity with the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Herbs|herbs]]\n| Pour a very thin layer of [[Salt|salt]] into a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] as near to the size of the [[Fish|fish]] as you can find - this uses less salt!\n| Lay the [[Fish|fish]] in the [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and completely cover with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| [[Bake]] the [[Fish|fish]] for 25 minutes.\n| When 20 minutes is nearly up, make the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Melt the [[Butter|butter]] in a small pan, add a grind of [[Pepper|pepper]] and the [[Zest|zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of a [[Lemon|lemon]], mix well.\n| Once the [[Fish|fish]] is cooked, the [[Salt|salt]] crust should lift off, together with the skin.  [[Brush|brush]] any reaming salt from the fish and serve, covered with the hot [[Sauce|sauce]] and a sprinkle of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[New Potatoes|new potatoes]] and [[Peas|peas]].\n===Variations===\nNormally I would have copious amounts of [[fennel]] or [[dill]] from the garden, but being January in England, I have none.  I will not pay good coin for a measly bunches of supermarket herbs so added three tablespoons of [[fennel seed]] to the [[sea salt]].  It was a good substitute, though fresh herbs would be better.\n===Chef's notes===\nI used 2 small [[bream]] instead of 1 large [[sea bass]] this time, both in the same salt-dish. It presents much better with just one fish - hence the lacking photographs!\n\nVery recently I saw Hugh Fearnley-Whittingstall cooking [[seabass]] in salt, he used a few kilograms of normal table salt, cleverly dampened down with little water to make a firm 'cement'.  Using this method packed the salt around his sea bass on a flat tray, rather like a jelly-mould of yester-year. It made a great table presentation.  I will try this next time.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #fishbakedinseasalt #seabass #bream #dill #sauce #fennel #lemon #parsley #france #bakingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Fougasse, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dough #yeast #flour #fougasse #bread #bake #baking #sieve #polenta #clingfilm #knead \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=My first attempt at these! This is based on a recipe in Richard Berthinet's Dough\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1629\n|PortionCalories = 407\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 4 fougasse\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 15 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 hours\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Fougasse recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Love this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looks SO funky!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nMy first attempt at these!  This is based on a recipe in  Richard Berthinet's '''[[Dough]]''' (ISBN 9781856267625).  I have started by making an overnight sponge, to encourage [[Yeast|yeast]] activity, but you can omit that stage if you like and mix in all the ingredients at the same time.   Excellent [[Bread|bread]] for tearing and dunking.\n\nSee 'Variations' below for instructions on how to partially make this in a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 10g fresh [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 350g [[Sparkling mineral water|sparkling mineral water]]\n| 500g strong [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]] - you may need to use more water if using very strong bread [[Flour|flour]]\n| 10g [[Salt|salt]]\n| [[Polenta]] for dusting\n\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| The night before you want to [[Bake|bake]] the [[Bread|bread]], dissolve the [[Yeast|yeast]] in the water,\n| [[Sieve]] 250g [[Flour|flour]] into a large bowl and stir in the water and dissolved [[Yeast|yeast]]. Do NOT add the [[Salt|salt]] at this stage as its will interfere with yeast activity.\n| Mix thoroughly.\n| Cover with [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]] and leave at room temperature overnight.\n| If it becomes very active, [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] and bring to room temperature in the morning.\n| The next day, [[Sieve|sieve]] the remaining 250g [[Flour|flour]] with the [[Salt|salt]] and add to the bowl.\n| Mix thoroughly and leave to rest for 20 minutes. \n| The [[Dough|dough]] should be fairly sticky, so add more water if necessary. \n| [[Knead]], using your desired method until you have an elastic [[Dough|dough]]. \n| Shape into a ball and leave it to rest for an hour in an oiled bowl, covered with [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]], until the [[Dough|dough]] has almost doubled in size.\n| Lightly [[Flour|flour]] a work surface with the [[polenta]] and gently deflate the [[Dough|dough]].  \n| [[Knead]] briefly and repeat the two previous steps, but do not vigorously deflate the [[Dough|dough]].\n| Divide into 4 equal pieces and shape into rectangles.\n| Make a large diagonal cut from the top right to the bottom left corner, without cutting into the corners.\n| Make at 3 or 4 diagonal cuts on each side of the first cut, again, without cutting right through to the edge.\n| Using your fingers, open the cuts right out.\n| Make sure the holes as are large as they will close up during [[Baking|baking]] and could converge ~(as mine did - see image above).\n| Slide onto a floured peel and then onto your [[Baking stone|baking stone]] or a floured [[Baking|baking]] sheet.\n| [[Bake]] at 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 210\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour] for 10-15 minutes until golden [[Brown|brown]].\n| Allow to cool on a wire rack.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nYou can do stages 6-12 in a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]], using the longest [[Dough|dough]] setting.   If you not making a sponge, then you can just add all the ingredients to the machine at the beginning.  You will also need to use just under a sachet of fast-action [[yeast]].\nFor the Panasonic SD253 breadmaker, use the French dough setting,  for the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]], use menu potion 08 French dough setting.\nPanasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #yeast #flour #fougasse #bread #bake #baking #sieve #polenta #clingfilm #knead </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

Should take about 5 to 10 minutes.\n| Lay the cooked legs onto kitchen paper to drain then arrange on a warm plate, surround with [[Lemons|lemons]] and sprinkle with [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Game recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#frogslegsinbreadcrumbs #breadcrumbs #flour #chicken #lemons #parsley #butter #oliveoil #egg #frogs #eggs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
