title": "Fumet",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Fumet; A French flavouring recipe Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fumet #stock #fish #sauces #sauce #poultry #recipes #chicken #soup #stocks #chickenstock \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=In cookery, this name is given to a number of different liquids which are used to flavour or add body to stocks and sauces\n|datePublished=2013-03-16\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n\n[[Image:Fish fumet.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Fish fumet]]\n\n===What is fumet===\nIn cookery, this name is given to a number of different liquids which are used to flavour or add body to [[stocks]] and [[sauces]].  Fumets are prepared by boiling foodstuffs of one kind or another in [[stock]] or wine.  They should not be confused with essences, extracts or concentrates.\n\n'''Chicken fumet''' is a kind of [[chicken]] [[soup]], made by boiling down very considerably a [[chicken stock]] which has been prepared in the usual way.  It is used to add flavour to various [[poultry]] dishes which are served with a [[sauce]].\n \n'''Fish fumet''' is used to add flavour to various [[fish]] dishes which are served with a [[sauce]].  It can also be made with red wine.\n\n* Add 125g finely chopped [[onions]], 150g pared [[mushrooms]], a [[bouquet garni]] and 10 drops of [[lemon juice]] to a stockpot.  \n* Cover with 2.5 kilos [[fish]] [[bones]] and trimmings.  \n* Add 10g [[salt]], 2.5 litres water and 500ml white wine.\n* Bring to the boil, skim and simmer gently for 30 minutes.\n* Strain through muslin or a fine sieve. \n\n'''Game fumet''' is a [[game]] [[stock]] (made with the carcasses and trimmings of different game) which is reduced to a more or less concentrated consistency, according to the flavour desired.\n\n'''Truffle fumet''' is used to enhance the flavour of certain [[sauces]] and is made by boiling down almost to nothing, a [[stock]] made by simmering [[truffle]] peelings in Madeira or any other fortified wine.  This [[stock]] is usually made when the [[truffles]] themselves are being used for some other purpose.\n\n\n[[Category:Cooking methods]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n{{CategoryLine}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n{{RecipeSkip}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#fumet #stock #fish #sauces #sauce #poultry #recipes #chicken #soup #stocks #chickenstock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

It's quite [[Garlic|garlic]]y but you'll probably know how much garlic is ''too much'' for you!\n\nIt only takes a few minutes to prepare, but is improved if left for a few hours for the flavours to minge, especially if you're out of season and using [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| Pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] - see [[Chef's notes]]\n| Pinch of pink seas [[Salt|salt]]\n| 6 good tablespoons of full-frat [[Greek yogurt]] (160 g)\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]] and [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to a bowl\n| Mix well with the back of a spoon\n| Stir in the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and optional [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| Mix well and leave to stand for a few hours if you have the time\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Garlic yogurt dip - ready to stand for 2 hours.jpg|Garlic dip, ready to stand for a few hours so the flavours can develop\nImage:Garlic yogurt dip - dried parsley added.jpg|A sprinkle of dried parsley will be re-hydrated in an hour or so\nImage:Garlic yogurt dip - spice ingredients.jpg|Garlic dip, the basic ingredients\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe as a [[Dip|dip]] for [[Chips|chips]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]]\n===Chef's notes===\nI pre-grind my ''special-mix'' [[black pepper]] and store in a covered bowl so it's easy to add a pinch, rather than having to grind it fresh each time. title": "Ginette Mathiot's Coq au vin",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ginette Mathiot's Coq au vin a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#butter #chicken #ginettemathiotscoqauvin #brandy #garlic #bacon #onions #diced #coqauvin #flour #potatoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Ginette Mathiot (1907-1998) was France's answer to Mrs Beeton, although she did not publish her book Je sais Cuisiner until 1932\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5660\n|PortionCalories = 943\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  13 hours\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  12 hours , 45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Ginette Mathiot's Coq au vin recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The old ones are the best - I can say that with truth now!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nGinette Mathiot (1907-1998) was [[France]]'s answer to Mrs Beeton, although she did not publish her book ''Je sais Cuisiner'' until 1932.  It has now been translated into English and is known as ''I know how to Cook'' (ISBN 0714848042).  \n\nThe recipe given below has been slightly adapted from Ginette's original.\n\nThis needs to be started the day before.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 90g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1.5kg [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, bone in (capon was traditionally used)\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], chopped\n| 40g [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 50ml [[Brandy|brandy]]\n| 500ml gutsy [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| Seasoning\n| 2 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and finely [[Diced|diced]] or chopped\n| 190g [[Button mushrooms|button mushrooms]], left whole, ot cut in half if on the large side\n| 100g [[Pickled|pickled]] silverskin [[Onions|onions]]\n| 100g [[Smoked bacon|smoked bacon]], [[Diced|diced]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| The day before you want to serve, heat the [[Oil|oil]] and 50g of the [[Butter|butter]] in a heavy pan or sauteuse.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and the [[Onion|onion]] and cook over a medium heat until the chicken is [[Browned|browned]] on both sides.\n| Sprinkle in the [[Flour|flour]] and stirring constantly, cook for a further few minutes.\n| Pour in the [[Brandy|brandy]] and the [[Wine|wine]], increase the heat, and cook until the aroma of [[Alcohol|alcohol]] has disappeared.\n| Season, add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook gently for one hour, turning over the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces half way through.\n| Cool and refrigerate overnight.\n| The next day, gently reheat over a low temperature.\n| Meanwhile, add the remaining 40g [[Butter|butter]] to a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Bacon|bacon]] until the [[Bacon|bacon]] is [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add to the [[Chicken|chicken]], leaving as much [[Butter|butter]] as possible in the [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Next, add the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] to the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and cook until softened.\n| Stir them into the [[Chicken|chicken]] and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Mashed|mashed]] or straw [[Potatoes|potatoes]].\n===Variations===\nYou can add other [[Vegetable|vegetable]] such as [[Carrots|carrots]] or [[Celery|celery]] if desired.\n===Chef's notes===\nIt was found be be very buttery, so I would recommend reducing the quantity of [[butter]].\n==See also==\n* [[Coq au vin]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #chicken #ginettemathiotscoqauvin #brandy #garlic #bacon #onions #diced #coqauvin #flour #potatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Gluten free red wine gravy recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#arrowroot #beefstock #honey #redonion #glutenfreeredwinegravy #gravy #blackpepper #vinegar #oliveoil #dairy #wheat \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This allergy free gravy recipe was created by Debbie&andrews sausages and Ceri Jones\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 364\n|PortionCalories = 60\n|DatePublished=22nd October 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  50 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Gluten free red wine gravy recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Coeliac's gravy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A nice gluten free gravy to pair with Debbie & Andrews gluten free sausage range.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Caramelised-red-onion-sausages.png|300px|thumb|right|[[Debbie & Andrew's Caramelised Red Onion Pork Sausages]]]]\nThis allergy free [[Gravy|gravy]] recipe was created by [[Debbie&andrew's sausages|debbie&andrew's sausages]] and natural chef, Ceri Jones. It is a perfect [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to their [[Debbie & Andrew's Caramelised Red Onion Pork Sausages|Caramelised Red onion Pork sausages]].\n\nThis recipe is [[Gluten free|gluten free]], [[Wheat|wheat]] free, [[Dairy|dairy]] free, does not contain [[Nut|nut]] or [[Soy|soy]].\n\nIt is reproduced courtesy of [[Debbie&andrew's sausages|debbie&andrew's sausages]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 teaspoon [[Honey|honey]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Balsamic vinegar|balsamic vinegar]] \n| 125mls [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 500mls [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[Arrowroot|arrowroot]], made into a thick paste (slurry) with 3 tablespoons water\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]]. Add the [[Red onion|red onion]] and cook on a low-medium heat for approximately 25 minutes, don\u0092t allow the [[Onions|onions]] to burn. After 25 minutes stir in a teaspoon of [[Honey|honey]] and cook for a further 5 minutes.\n| Next, turn up the heat and pour in the [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Wine|wine]] and [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], then reduce heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes.\n| Finally add the [[Arrowroot|arrowroot]] slurry, and stir well to thicken the [[Gravy|gravy]].\n| Add a good twist of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] then taste and add [[Salt|salt]] if necessary. If your [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] is already [[Salted|salted]] you won\u0092t need any more.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Arrowroot]] is added at the end of cooking. If it overheats, its thickening powers will be obliterated.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#arrowroot #beefstock #honey #redonion #glutenfreeredwinegravy #gravy #blackpepper #vinegar #oliveoil #dairy #wheat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is brought to [[Cookipedia]] courtesy of debbiesandandrews [[Sausages|sausages]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 Pack of [[Debbie and Andrew's Harrogate 97% Gluten Free Pork Sausages]]\n| 2tbs [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 200g [[Smoked|smoked]] [[Lardons|lardons]]\n| 1 [[Brown|brown]] [[Onion|onion]], [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 [[Carrots|carrots]], [[Diced|diced]]\n| 2 [[Celery|celery]] sticks, [[Diced|diced]]\n| 1 [[Sweet potato|sweet potato]], cubed\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, minced|cloves garlic, minced]]\n| 10 [[Sage leaves|sage leaves]] - roughly chopped\n| &#189; bottle of [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 400g can [[Cannellini beans|cannellini beans]] - drained and rinsed\n| 400g can of chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2tbs [[Honey|honey]]\n| 50g [[Gluten free|gluten free]] [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Use a large, stove-top and [[Oven|oven]] friendly dish. Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Red wine|red wine]] and cook out for 5 minutes until reduced by half.\n| Add your [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Cannellini beans|cannellini beans]], [[Honey|honey]] and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste.\n| Place the debbie&andrew's [[Harrogate 97% Pork Sausages]] carefully on top being careful not to fully submerge as you want the [[Sausages|sausages]] to get a lovely golden [[Brown|brown]] colour.\n| Sprinkle with [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]], drizzle with a little extra [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and lay a few extra whole [[Sage leaves|sage leaves]] on the top.\n| Place in the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 40 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with crusty [[Gluten free|gluten free]] [[Bread|bread]].\n===See also===\n* [[Udi's Gluten Free Products|Udi\u0092s Gluten Free Products for gluten free bread]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#glutenfree #glutenfreesausagecassoulet #oliveoil #diced #sausages #breadcrumbs #cannellinibeans #lardons #celery #honey #sweetpotato </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You are now, but a very distant memory, but your griddle-pan waffles will live on in perpetuity. --JP</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n[https://www.facebook.com/samhardacre Sam Hardacre] one of [http://themarketinglab.co.uk/ The Marketing Lab's] array of Geek Brains, brought this rather clever idea to my attention and also provided the picture, thanks Sam.\n\nIt does not require a [[Waffle maker]] and can made with a normal stove-top griddle pan.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| 300 ml [[Buttermilk|buttermilk]] or [[Semi-skimmed milk|semi-skimmed milk]]\n| See this [[buttermilk]] link for how to make your own buttermilk from regular [[milk]]\n| 225 g (8 oz) [[Self-raising flour|self-raising flour]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Table salt|table salt]]\n| 100g [[Butter|butter]] , softened in the [[Microwave|microwave]] for a few seconds\n| 1tsp extra [[Butter|butter]] for cooking\n| Optional for sweet waffles: \n| &#189; tsp. [[Vanilla extract|vanilla extract]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Pre heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3) if you are making lots so they can be kept warm\n* Get the [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] nice and hot before [[Hand|hand]] as some cast [[Iron|iron]] pans can take a while to get hot.\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Whisk the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Eggs|eggs]] in a large bowl\n| Using a fine [[Sieve|sieve]], sift the [[Flour|flour]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Baking powder|baking powder]] into the [[Egg|egg]]-mix.\n| Fold the softened [[Butter|butter]] into the mixture. Mix this just enough to combine the ingredients.  Jamie Oliver advises not to over-mix at this stage or the waffles will not puff up.\n| Add the extra teaspoons of [[Butter|butter]] to the pan and [[Brush|brush]] or swill to coat evenly.\n| Immediately pour the mixture into the pan over a medium heat  and carefully tip it to spread and cover the whole of the pan as you would with a [[Pancake|pancake]]\n| Cook for 8 to 10 minutes on this side, or until golden, then  then flip the waffle and cook for another 8 to 10 minutes on this side\n| If you are making lots then keep them warm in the [[Oven|oven]], but don't stack them of they will [[Sweat|sweat]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nCrispy [[Bacon|bacon]], sliced [[Avocado|avocado]] and [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]]\n\n[[Red onion]], [[Black olives|black olives]], and [[Feta cheese]]\n\n[[Butter]], [[Banana|banana]], [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]], and [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n\n[[Maple syrup]]\n\n[[Honey]]\n\n[[Chocolate sauce]] and squirty [[Cream|cream]]\n===Recipe source===\n\n* http://www.jamieoliver.com/recipes/eggs-recipes/griddle-pan-waffles\n==See also==\n{{SeeAlso-Waffles}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Australian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #griddlepanwaffles #buttermilk #banana #freerangeeggs #hand #fetacheese #avocado #wafflemaker #chocolatesauce #pancake </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

oz) [[Butter|butter]], softened in the Basque evening sun.\n| 1 teaspoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].\n| 1 tablespoon [[White wine|white wine]] or [[Lager|lager]], or whatever...\n| 2 tablespoons [[Parsley|parsley]], chopped finely.\n| 1 tablespoon [[Chives|chives]], chopped finely.\n| 1 450g can very well rinsed white [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]] or [[Flageolet|flageolet]] vert.\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste.\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Mash]] the [[Butter|butter]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].  Season well and reserve.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] slowly in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] until softened, but without [[Brown|brown]]ing them.\n| Add the [[White wine|white wine]] to the [[Onions|onions]], then add the rinsed and drained [[Beans|beans]] and heat gently.\n| Add the [[Herb|herb]] [[Butter|butter]] and fold in to melt and mix well.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot\n===variations===\nAlmost any cooked beans would work with this recipe.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #haricotsblancsaubeurremaitredhotel #lemonjuice #onions #oliveoil #whitewine #garlic #haricotbeans #flageolet #whitebeans #beans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Home-made Camembert cheese",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Home-made Camembert cheese, French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#doublecream #dried #freeze #mould #fat #cheese #homemadecamembertcheese #curd #curds #frenchrecipescamembertcheese #cutthecurds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=You need to prepare the freeze dried Penicillium 24 hours in advance of making the Camembert cheese\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}} \n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3375\n|PortionCalories = 210\n|DatePublished=14th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Vegetable steamer as mould - centre removed\n |Servings = Servings: 16 - Makes 600 g of finished [[Cheese|cheese]]\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 1 day\n |PrepTime = 1 day plus maturation period\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Vegetable steamer as cheese mould.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">'''Hard work!'''</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A lot of work involved, just to make your own cheese, but well worth the effort.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n==Prepare 24 hours in advance!==\nRemember, you need to prepare the freeze dried [[Penicillium Roquefortii]] 24 hours in advance of making the cheese.  I always forget.\n\nWell, Cottage, [[Cheddar]], [[Caerphilly]] and [[Stilton]] worked out very well so now it's time to try making [[Camembert cheese]] at home.  As with the last few that I've made, I am using full-[[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]] and adding [[Double cream|double cream]] for that rich, creamy, high-[[cholesterol]] effect!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[Litres|litres]] full [[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 300 ml [[Double cream|double cream]]\n| 5 ml [[Liquid starter|liquid starter]] or a little [[Freeze|freeze]]-[[Dried|dried]] [[DVI starter]] (as much as will go on the tip of a pointed knife - see picture) \n| 3 drops of [[Rennet|rennet]]\n| A little [[Freeze|freeze]]-[[Dried|dried]] Penicillium culture (as much as will go on the tip of a pointed knife - see picture)\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Sterilise]] all equipment\n* Add 3 drops of [[Rennet|rennet]] to 1 tablespoon of cold, previously [[Boiled|boiled]] water, mix well.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:DoubleBoiler.jpg|Use a double boiler so you don't scald the milk\nImage:Knife-tip-DVI.jpg|DVI - Knife-tips worth\nImage:Knife-tip-Candidum.jpg|Penicillum candidum - Knife-tips worth\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using [[Unpasteurised|unpasteurised]] [[Milk|milk]], pasteurise and allow to cool, add the [[Double cream|double cream]] and stabilise at 29\u00b0 C\n| If using shop-bought [[Milk|milk]], add the [[Double cream|double cream]] and adjust the temperature to  29\u00b0 C.\n| Add the [[Freeze|freeze]] [[Dried|dried]] [[DVI]] and the Penicillium culture by sprinkling on the surface of the [[Milk|milk]] and whisking well.\n| After 30 minutes check the temperature is still 29\u00b0 C, add the diluted [[Rennet|rennet]], cover and leave until the [[Curd|curd]] has set, ensuring the temperature remains constant.  I find covering with a few towels [[Help|help]]s keep retain the temperature.\n| Once the [[Curd|curd]] has set, don't [[Cut the curds|cut the curds]] with a knife, but ladle, in large slices directly into the [[Mould|mould]].\n| Leave to drain at 20\u00b0.  When the [[Curds|curds]] are firm, turn upside-down and continue draining.  This entire process may take a day or so.\n| When the [[Curds|curds]] are firm enough to remove from the [[Mould|mould]], rub with a fine dusting of [[Salt|salt]].\n| Transfer to a [[Drying|drying]] area (18\u00b0 C / 80% humidity) for 2 days.\n| Then move to a ripening area (around 12\u00b0 C / 80% humidity) for about 10 days or more, by which time the [[Mould|mould]] should have formed.\n| Unless you have a cave handy, the [[fridge]] is probably the best place to mature your [[homemade cheese]] although it's really going to be too cold. After discovering the top shelf of my often-opened fridge could be as much as 5\u00b0 C warmer than the bottom, I've decided to mature my cheeses there.  As all fridges differ, check various areas of your fridge with a thermometer to find the area that is around 11\u00b0C [51\u00b0 F], the ideal 'cave' temperature.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nWhen trying to stabilise the temperature, take your time and don't rush or you will almost certainly overheat the [[Milk|milk]] and spoil your [[Cheese|cheese]].\n\nIt's quite useful, once you think you have stabilised the [[Milk|milk]] at a certain temperature, to leave if for 30 minutes and then check the temperature again before starting your [[Cheese making|cheese making]].\n\nDusting with [[Salt|salt]]:  I find that I use less salt but get a more even covering if I dust with salt that has been [[Ground|ground]] to a very fine powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] first.\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Camembert cheese]]\n[[Category:Cheese making|Camembert cheese]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Camembert cheese]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Camembert cheese]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#doublecream #dried #freeze #mould #fat #cheese #homemadecamembertcheese #curd #curds #frenchrecipescamembertcheese #cutthecurds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

If you cook this with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] you have a complete meal.\n\nFinish off with lashings of [[balsamic vinegar gravy]] or Jamie Oliver's [[Hot mint and caper sauce|hot mint and caper sauce]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g leg of [[Lamb|lamb]] (about half a log)\n| 4 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled and thinly sliced, lengthways\n| 10 [[Anchovy fillets|anchovy fillets]], cut in half, widthways\n| 3 whole [[Rosemary#Sprigs of rosemary|sprigs of rosemary]], remove the leaves of one and chop roughly\n| 1 [[Carrot|carrot]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 [[Parsnip|parsnip]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 [[Leek|leek]], trimmed and cut into thick rings \n| 2 big [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and quartered\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], bruised\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to it's hottest setting.\n* [[Blanch]] the [[Leek|leek]] in [[Boiling|boiling]] water and leave soaking for 10 minutes\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roasted vegetables.jpg|Vegetables roasted\nImage:Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies ready.jpg|Ready to rumble\nImage:Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies ingredients.jpg|The basics\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Using a small sharp paring knife carefully stab the [[Lamb|lamb]], making deep incisions all over\n| Push the [[Garlic|garlic]] slices, [[Anchovies|anchovies]] and chopped [[Rosemary|rosemary]] into the incisions\n| Line the base of a large [[roasting tray]] with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and drizzle with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Cut all of the vegetables into equal-sized chunks so they will cook evenly\n| Season the [[Lamb|lamb]] with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], place on top of the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and sprinkle with the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and lay the other sprigs of rosemary on top of the lamb\n| '''Reduce the heat to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)''' - this way the oven starts off really hot to sear the meat but quickly cools to roast at the correct temperature.\n| Put a smaller empty [[roasting tray]] in to heat to finish off the [[vegetables]]\n| [[Roast]] the [[Lamb|lamb]] for 30 to 40 minutes, once it is cooked to you liking, remove, keep warm and rest while the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are completed.\n| Move the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] to the smaller tray and cook until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are golden [[Brown|brown]] - about 20 minutes more\n| If making the [[Hot caper sauce]], use the original [[roasting tray]] for this, then you can use all of the lovely juices\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice and serve with the [[Roast|roast]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[hot caper sauce]]\n===Variations===\nThis is a great recipe for using up any odd vegetables.  Most supermarkets offer quite reasonably priced stew-packs that have a pretty good variety of vegetables, ideal for this dish.\n===Chef's notes===\nBuying [[Frozen lamb - what great value!|frozen lamb for this dish]] makes it really economical (only \u00a36.00 per kilogram 2013)\n==See also==\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]  \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vegetables #lambwithgarlicrosemaryandanchovies #lamb #garlic #roastingtray #roast #leek #hotcapersauce #rosemary #anchovies #potatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

And, [[Hollandaise|hollandaise]] without whisking - genius!\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 [[duck|duck egg]] or 2 chicken [[eggs]] per person\n| 6 [[Asparagus spears|asparagus spears]]\n| 100g pack of [[Pancetta|pancetta]], [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]] or [[Parma ham|parma ham]]\n| A knob of [[Butter|butter]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| A drop of [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]] (optional)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Get your [[Eggs|eggs]] so they can warm to room temp. Crank your [[Oven grill|oven grill]] up to high.\n| Snap or slice the woody ends off the [[Asparagus|asparagus]]. Wrap each spear with a slice of [[Pancetta|pancetta]] or a halved (lengthwise) strip of [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]] or [[Parma ham|parma ham]].\n| Get a pot of water on the [[Boil|boil]] for the [[Eggs|eggs]].\n| Pop the wrapped spears on a hot [[Grill pan|grill pan]] and under the [[Grill|grill]]. Add a drop of [[Vinegar|vinegar]] to give a lazy [[Hollandaise|hollandaise]]-y effect. Dunk.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n{{Template:Abel and Cole veg box recipes attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#eggs #butter #boil #lazyhollandaiseyasparagus #pancetta #parmaham #hollandaise #prosciutto #ham #ovengrill #duck </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe uses the oven. Baking them produces an excellent crouton\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 266\n|PortionCalories = 33\n|DatePublished=12th July 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Making crispy croutons for salads recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Use stale bread</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for using up left-over bread and rolls.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Croutons]] are a great way to liven up any [[Salad|salad]] and are really easy to make at home.  They can be made on the [[Croutons recipe|hob, in a frying pan]], but I've found the best results are achieved if you make them in the [[Oven|oven]] as they get a nice even crisp and you don't have to fiddle about with them too much.\n\nThe [[Croutons|croutons]] will stay nice and crispy for at least a month if kept in a [[Lock and Lock]] style box once they have been allowed to cool down.\n\n[[French]] [[Baguettes|baguettes]] make the best [[Croutons|croutons]], but I've yet to find a decent [[Baguette|baguette]] outside [[France]].  [[Ciabatta bread]] or rolls have a similar texture and give very good results.\n\nTwo [[Ciabatta|ciabatta]] rolls make enough to garnish a [[Salad|salad]] for eight people.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Ciabatta|ciabatta]] rolls\n| A good splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| A shake of [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]]\n| Fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5).  In this instance, the fan oven temperature can be the same.  Just watch them carefully!\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Salad croutons.jpg|Croutons after baking to 10 minutes\nImage:Croutons oiled, seasoned and ready for the oven.jpg|Oiled, seasoned and ready for baking\nImage:Ciabatta bread cut into croutons.jpg|Two rolls make enough croutons to serve eight people\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Cut the [[Bread|bread]] into similar sized cubes\n| Spread the [[Croutons|croutons]] out on the [[Oven tray|oven tray]]\n| [[Spray]] or sprinkle a few tablespoons f [[Olive oil|olive oil]] over the [[Croutons|croutons]]\n| Season with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and a shake of [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]]\n| Use a silicone [[Brush|brush]] to ensure the [[Croutons|croutons]] are evenly coated with the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and distribute them evenly on the tray\n| [[Bake]] for 5 minutes in the top of the [[Oven|oven]]\n| After 5 minutes turn them and [[Bake|bake]] the [[Croutons|croutons]] for a further 5 minutes.  Check them often as they can burn easily.\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]] and leave to cool on the tray\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nUse the [[Croutons|croutons]] to garnish [[Soups|soups]] or [[Salads|salads]].\n\nThese apparently make a great [[Snacks|snack]] - the pile gets smaller and smaller every time someone walks through the kitchen!\n===Variations===\nUse flavoured [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n\nAdd a few sprigs of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] to the tray to flavour the [[Croutons|croutons]]\n\n[[Herb]] [[Bread|bread]], [[Cheese|cheese]] [[Breads|breads]] make an interesting change\n\n{{Template:Croutons recipes}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#croutons #oliveoil #makingcrispycroutonsforsalads #bread #bake #salad #ciabatta #mixedherbs #miseenplace #france #spray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

seasoned\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and quartered\n| A pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| 2 tablespoons [[Flour|flour]]\n| 1 litre [[Meat stock|meat stock]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e or 100g freshly pulped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 [[Bouquet garni for mutton|bouquet garni]]\n| 400g [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and chopped into pieces the size of large [[Olives|olives]]\n| 24 small pickling [[Onions|onions]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a deep pan.\n| Add the seasoned [[Mutton|mutton]] and the [[Onion|onion]].\n| When the [[Mutton|mutton]] cubes are well [[Seared|seared]], pour of some of the [[Fat|fat]].\n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]] and cook until the [[Onion|onion]] begins to caramelise.\n| Stir and the [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook briefly - do not allow it to burn\n| Mix in the [[Flour|flour]], hot [[Stock|stock]], [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e or pulped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and the [[Bouquet garni for mutton|bouquet garni]].\n| Cover, and cook gently for an hour.\n| Meanwhile, heat a little oil in a pan, add the pickling [[Onions|onions]] and a large pinch of [[sugar]].\n| Cook until the [[onions]] are caramelised and set aside.\n| At the end of the cooking time for the [[mutton]], add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and pickling [[Onions|onions]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and allow to [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are cooked.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a bowl of seasonal [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#mutton #onions #navarindemoutonauxpommesdeterre #onion You bread maker must have a 'French bake' setting for this to work.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nWe have been using [[Breadmakers|breadmakers]] for about ten years now, I think we're on our third now.  We now [[Bake|bake]] [[Bread|bread]] every two days and we have come up with a recipe that never fails to make a light airy loaf.\n\nWe add a little bit of [[Wholemeal flour|wholemeal flour]], just for a little interest, but not enough to make a heavy loaf.\n\nWe've made this in a variety of [[Panasonic Breadmakers]] which all have a 'French bake' setting.  This is an extended rise and gives a very light airy loaf.  You cannot make an extra large loaf with this setting as it rises too much.  it would probably work on a normal setting if your breadmaker does not have 'French bake'.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 teaspoon Allinson's Easy [[Bake]] [[Yeast]] - See [[Chef's notes|chef's notes]] below for other types of yeast.\n| 200g [[Strong white flour|strong white flour]]\n| 200g [[Strong brown flour|strong brown flour]]\n| 2 pinches of [[Ascorbic acid|ascorbic acid]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Salt|salt]]\n| 20g [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 280g water\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Although the instructions say to put the [[Yeast|yeast]] in the separate compartment, we always tip everything together in the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] bin.  It's up to you.\n| If you are not using a fast [[Easy Bake Yeast]] , then '''activate it first''' - [[How to activate Allinsons Dried Active Yeast|'''instructions are here''']].\n| Set the breadmaker to 'French Bake'  setting (#8 on the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502]])\n| Your loaf should be ready after 6 hours.  Put a timer on so you don;t forget it as it will collapse if you leave it in the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] for an extended period after if has completed the [[Baking|baking]] cycle.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nCategory:Favourite recipes\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you do buy [[Allinsons Dried Active Yeast]] and want to use it in a [[breadmaker]] you need to '''activate it first''' - [[How to activate Allinsons Dried Active Yeast|'''instructions are here''']].\n\nWe ''always'' use [[olive oil]] in our [[breadmaking]] as we don't keep standard [[vegetable oil]] anymore.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#breadmaker #howtoactivateallinsonsdriedactiveyeast #yeast #vegetableoil #bake #bread #breadmaking #ascorbicacid #easybakeyeast #strongwhiteflour #grainandbeanrecipes</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This version also contains spelt flour\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1890\n|PortionCalories = 189\n|DatePublished=8th March 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Pain de Campagne\n |Servings = Servings: 10 - Makes 1 loaf\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 5 hours 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 hours\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Learning to use a brotform.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Complex</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But worth the effort</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nAs this recipe has no 'mother dough', it is quicker to make than [[Pain de Campagne (Country Bread)]]. This version also contains [[Spelt|spelt]] [[Flour|flour]].  For this recipe, the [[Dough|dough]] is made in a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] but the [[Bread|bread]] is [[Baked|baked]] in the [[Oven|oven]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons easy-blend [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 300 g [[French bread]] [[Flour|flour]] or strong, plain [[Bread|bread]] flour\n| 150 g [[Spelt|spelt]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 50 g [[Rye flour|rye flour]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 25 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 350 ml [[Milk|milk]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the ingredients into the [[Bread maker|bread maker]] in the order specified in your instruction manual.  The above order is correct for the [[Panasonic SD253]], SD254 and SD255.\n| If you have one, set to [[French bread]] programme; if not, set to the programme which has the longest rising time.  This is menu option 08 for the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]]\n| One the process has finished, knock the [[Dough|dough]] back and place, seam side uppermost, in a lightly oiled, well floured [[Banneton|banneton]] basket.\n| Leave in a [[warm place]], covered with a damp [[Tea-towel|tea-towel]] until double its size.\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7) - if you wish for a crispy crust, place a bowl of water in the oven at this time.\n| Grease a [[Baking|baking]] sheet or line it with [[Bake-O-Glide]].\n| When the [[Dough|dough]] has risen, place the [[Baking|baking]] sheet, upside down, on top of the [[banneton]] basket.\n| Quickly, but carefully, flip the whole thing over so that the [[Dough|dough]] is now on the [[baking tray]].\n| Place in the [[Oven|oven]] immediately and allow to [[Bake|bake]] for 10-15 minutes.\n| Reduce the temperature to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5) and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 15-20 minutes until the [[Bread|bread]] sounds hollow when tapped.\n}}\n===Variations===\nYou can make the whole thing in the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] if you wish and shape it any way you like, although you may need to adjust the cooking time and temperature if making a long loaf.\n===Chef's notes===\nFrom what I can establish, the best combination of [[flours]] to use for flouring the [[banneton]] is half [[rice flour]] and half ordinary [[plain flour]].  For this recipe, I used the [[rye]] blade in the machine.  This was purely because I had 'lost' the normal blade - which I eventually realised was still in the [[Ballymaloe brown bread]] that I had made the day before! I am sure a normal blade would be fine as half of the [[flour]] is [[wheat flour]].  \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pain de campagne (2)]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pain de campagne (2)]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes|Pain de campagne (2)]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Pain de campagne (2)]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Pain de campagne (2)]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#flour #dough #breadmaker #bread #banneton #baking #bake #spelt #frenchbread #warmplace #ballymaloebrownbread </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pain de Campagne (Country Bread)",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pain de Campagne (Country Bread) a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dough #breadmaker #bread #ryeflour #frenchbread #strongwhiteflour #baking #driedyeast #flour #tinfoil #flours \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe for a French country bread is an adaptation (for use with a breadmaker) of a Spanish recipe at Gastronomia y Cia\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2265\n|PortionCalories = 755\n|DatePublished=22nd October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 3 small or 2 large loaves\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 10 hours 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 hours\n |CookTime = 50 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Pain de Campagne (Country Bread).jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Big, round bread.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Trousers!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis recipe for a [[French]] country [[Bread|bread]] is an adaptation (for use with a [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]]) of a Spanish recipe at '''[http://www.gastronomiaycia.com/?s=Pain+de+Campagne&x=15&y=13 Gastronomia y Cia.]'''.  I made this using a Pansasonic SD-255.  Start making the [[bread]] the day before you wish to eat it.\n\n\n'''Mother [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 380 g [[French bread]] [[Flour|flour]] or [[Strong white flour|strong white flour]]\n| 100 g wholewheat [[Rye flour|rye flour]]\n| 325 ml water - or by weight instead of volume, 325 g water\n| 5 g Easy Blend [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]]\n| 8 g [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n'''[[Bread]] [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 260 g [[French bread]] [[Flour|flour]] or [[Strong white flour|strong white flour]]\n| 55 g wholewheat [[Rye flour|rye flour]]\n| 175 ml water - or by weight instead of volume, 175g water\n| 4 g Easy Blend [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]]\n| 4 g [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''The mother [[Dough|dough]] is made first.'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the mother [[Dough|dough]] ingredients to the pan of your [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] in the order specified in the manufacturer's instructions.\n| If the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] has a [[French bread]] [[Dough|dough]] only setting, use that.  If it does not, then use the longest dough programme available.  For the [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] this is menu option 21, French dough.\n| Allow the [[Dough|dough]] to rise in the pan for a minimum of 6 hours in the [[breadmaker]] or place it overnight in a [[Fridge|fridge]], in which case, remove from the fridge 2 hours before making the [[Bread|bread]] dough.  \n}}\n'''We now make the [[Bread|bread]] [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Bread|bread]] [[Dough|dough]] ingredients to the mother dough in the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] and set to the same programme that you used for the mother dough.\n| Allow the [[Dough|dough]] to rise until double its size.\n| Remove from the [[Breadmaker|breadmaker]] and place on a floured board.\n| Knead and divide the mixture into two or three equal parts and shape as desired. \n| Place the loaves on [[Baking|baking]] tins, cover and leave again until doubled in size.\n| Meanwhile, preheat the [[Oven|oven]] at the highest temperature and at the same time place a bowl or tray of water on the bottom.\n| When the loaves have risen, put them in the [[Oven|oven]] and immediately reduce the temperature to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7).\n| Should the loaves become too [[Brown|brown]] during [[Baking|baking]], cover them with [[Tin foil|tin foil]].\n| Allow to [[Bake|bake]] for 30-35 minutes, remove from [[Oven|oven]] and allow to cool on a cake rack.\n}}\n===Variations===\nTry substituting the [[Rye flour|rye flour]] with [[Spelt|spelt]], [[Kamut|kamut]] or any other [[Flours|flours]].  \n\nIf you want to bake the whole thing in the [[breadmaker]], reduce the ingredients by a third or a half and follow the manufacturer's instructions.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou might feel that this is a long winded way of making [[Bread|bread]], but the idea of having a mother [[Dough|dough]] is to improve the flavour and texture of the bread.  It also improves its keeping qualities.\n\nAlso, please ensure that you use the correct quantity of [[rye flour]] as it absorbs more water than ordinary [[strong white flour|bread flour]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pain de campagne (country bread)]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pain de campagne (country bread)]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes|Pain de campagne (country bread)]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Pain de campagne (country bread)]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Pain de campagne (country bread)]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #breadmaker #bread #ryeflour #frenchbread #strongwhiteflour #baking #driedyeast #flour #tinfoil #flours </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoons easy-[[Blend|blend]] [[Yeast|yeast]] or 10g fresh yeast\n| 370g [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 25 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 300 g [[French bread]] [[Flour|flour]] or strong, plain [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 150 g [[Spelt|spelt]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 50 g [[Rye flour|rye flour]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Yeast|yeast]], [[Milk|milk]] [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Butter|butter]] to the TM bowl.\n| Mix for '''2 minutes / Temp. 37\u00b0 / Speed 1'''.\n| Add the remaining ingredients in the order given above.\n| '''4 minutes / [[Knead]]'''\n| Leave in the TM bowl until the [[Dough|dough]] has rested and is touching the lid.\n| '''12 seconds / [[Knead]]'''\n| Tip the TM bowl upside down on a lightly floured surface .\n| Loosen the blades by undoing the blade unit at the base. The weight of the blades will [[Help|help]] the [[Dough|dough]] to drop out of the bowl onto the surface.\n| Pull any remaining bits of [[Dough|dough]] off the blades and out of the TM bowl.\n| Shape into a ball, place in an oiled bowl and cover with [[Cling-film|cling-film]] or a shower cap.\n| Leave until the [[Dough|dough]] has almost doubled in size (about an hour).\n| Knock the [[Dough|dough]] back and place, seam side uppermost, in a lightly oiled, well floured [[Banneton|banneton]] basket.\n| Leave in a [[warm place]], covered with [[Cling-film|cling-film]] or shower cap until double its size.\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to '''220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)''' - if you wish for a crispy crust, place a bowl of water in the oven at this time.\n| Grease a [[Baking|baking]] sheet or line it with [[Bake-O-Glide]] you can also use a preheated [[Baking stone|baking stone]], dusted with [[Semolina|semolina]], in which case you will need a peel to transfer the [[Bread|bread]].\n| When the [[Dough|dough]] has risen, place the [[Baking|baking]] sheet, upside down, on top of the [[Banneton|banneton]] basket.\n| Quickly, but carefully, flip the whole thing over so that the [[Dough|dough]] is now on the [[Baking tray|baking tray]].\n| Place in the [[Oven|oven]] immediately and allow to [[Bake|bake]] for 20 minutes.\n| Reduce the temperature to '''190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5)''' and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 20-25 minutes until the [[Bread|bread]] sounds hollow when tapped.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nFrom what I can establish, the best combination of [[Flours|flours]] to use for flouring the [[Banneton|banneton]] is half [[Rice flour|rice flour]] or [[Semolina|semolina]] and half ordinary [[Plain flour|plain flour]].  I always [[Oil|oil]] the banneton before flouring and line it with a hair net (helps the [[Dough|dough]] to be easily released from the basket).  This can also be [[Baked|baked]] in a 1kg loaf tin.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #bread #flour #banneton #knead #semolina #bake #baking #yeast #butter #thermomix </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pasta thermidor a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pastathermidor #tarragon #butter #driedspaghetti #parsley #grill #cheese #onions #parmesancheese #drysherry #sherry \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Posh macaroni cheese! This is such a great recipe that it is worth making your own pasta if you have the time\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2529\n|PortionCalories = 1264\n|DatePublished=22nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime =  30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Pasta thermidor.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">No fish, just flavours</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I expected this to have lots of lobster or prawns but it's just sauce and pasta. Odd but good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nPosh [[macaroni cheese]]!\n[[Image:Pasta thermidor ready for the grill.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready for the grill]]\n\nThis is such a great recipe that it is worth making your own pasta if you have the time.  You don't need a special pasta cutter, just roll it out and slash it into strips.  However, this will still be good with [[dried spaghetti]] or [[Gallery_of_pasta_types|pasta]].\n\n\n'''Thermidor sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 50 g (2 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Onion|onion]] or [[shallots]], finely chopped\n| 3 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]]\n| 3 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 275 ml (1/2 pint) full [[Cream|cream]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 5 tablespoons (60  ml) [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n| pinch of [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]] (not [[Smoked|smoked]])\n| pinch of [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]]\n| 5 tablespoons of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]]\n| grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n}}\n'''Pasta'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 portion of fresh pasta - [[Pasta|make it yourself, the recipe is easy]].\n}}\nor\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200g [[Dried spaghetti]] or [[pasta]] (100g per person)\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n===Method===\n\n\n'''pasta'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add  to lightly salted boiling water and boil:\n| 3 to 5 minutes (fresh pasta)\n| 7-10 minutes (dried spaghetti / thin pasta)\n| 10-13 minutes (thicker pasta)\n| There is a [[Pasta_cooking_times|detailed list of pasta cooking times here]].\n| Drain well and add a dash of olive oil and mix well to prevent sticking\n}}\n'''sauce'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Melt half of the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan and gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] until translucent.\n| Add the [[Flour|flour]], mix into a [[Roux|roux]] and then gradually stir in the [[milk]].  Whisking will quickly remove any  lumps.\n| Add the [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Tarragon|tarragon]].\n| Mix in the [[Sherry|sherry]] and [[Spices|spices]], season to taste and adjust to your liking.\n| Add the remaining [[Butter|butter]] and half of the [[Cheese|cheese]].  Mix well.\n| Mix in the cooked pasta. Spoon the mixture into a lightly greased baking tray.\n| Sprinkle with the remaining [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Brown|brown]] under the [[Grill|grill]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nAdd lots of Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] with the [[Onions|onions]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are struggling to get hold of fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]], at a push you could add 1 heaped teaspoon of [[dried tarragon]] to a little [[Boiled|boiled]] water, allow it to rehydrate, drain any liquid and then use, however, fresh is plainly better.\n==See also==\n* [[Lobster thermidor]]\n* [[Prawn thermidor]]\n* [[Thermidor sauce]]\n\n{{Template:YoutubePastaDough}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pastathermidor #tarragon #butter #driedspaghetti #parsley #grill #cheese #onions #parmesancheese #drysherry #sherry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe is quick and easy to prepare and very easy to adapt so it suits your personal taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 large [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]], plus extra for drizzling\n| 150g (5oz) [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]], [[defrosted]]\n| 1 large [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 4 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sherry|sherry]] or [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 150g (5oz) wholemeal [[Bread|bread]], crumbled. \n| Pinch of [[Chili flakes|chili flakes]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Slice off the tops, leaving the stem intact; reserve.\n| With deft knife-work, remove the white membranes and knock out the [[Seeds|seeds]].\n| Heat the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and flavour it with a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Slightly crush the [[Peas|peas]] so they can really absorb the [[Garlic|garlic]] [[Oil|oil]].\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes, add the [[Peas|peas]] and saut\u00e9 for a further 4 minutes.\n| Soak the crumbled [[Bread|bread]] in the [[Sherry|sherry]] and then stir into cooked [[Peas|peas]] and [[Onions|onions]].\n| Remove from the heat.\n| Season the insides of the [[Peppers|peppers]] with [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and a sprinkling of [[Chili flakes|chili flakes]].\n| Distribute the [[Pea|pea]] mixture between the [[Peppers|peppers]]. Drizzle with a little more [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| Replace the tops and [[Bake|bake]] for 25 minutes.\n}}\n===Variations===\nA little finely [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan]] mixed in with the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] adds an extra lift to this dish.\n==See also==\n* [[Cheese, peas and garlic stuffed peppers]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #peaandgarlicstuffedpeppers #peas #oliveoil #bread #peppers #chiliflakes #sherry #onions #seeds #pea </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Persillade",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Persillade, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#persillade #parsley #oliveoil #miseenplace #garlic #breadcrumbs #gremolata #potatoes #panfried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Persillade is the culinary term for a chopped mixture of garlic and parsley, usually in equal parts by volume\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 344\n|PortionCalories = 86\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 15 minutes incl chill time\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Persillade.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Garlicky parsley</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.9</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Parsley and garlic are soulmates.  I always use them together so this is hardly new to me.  Try it!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Persillade''' is the culinary term for a chopped mixture of [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[parsley]], usually in equal parts by volume. The root of the word is persil, the French word for [[parsley]]. Simple to make, but a common ingredient in many dishes, it is often included in a saut\u00e9 cook's [[mise en place]]. It can be added early in a dish for a mellow flavour, added at the very end of the cooking to provide a garlicky jolt, or even used raw as a garnish.\n\nA classic French bistro dish is [[Pommes persillade]], basically cubed [[potatoes]] fried in small amount of oil, with persillade added at the end of the cooking. New Orleans chef Austin Leslie's signature dish was Fried Chicken with Persillade--basically fried chicken with the garlic and parsley mixture added as a garnish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| 1 [[garlic clove, crushed]]\n| 1 cup [[breadcrumbs]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[parsley]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[olive oil]] in a frying pan, add the garlic and breadcrumbs and stir-fry for a minute or so, then combine with the parsley.\n| Allow to cool and serve.\n}}\n===Chef's note===\nThis can be made without the breadcrumbs, depending on the dish it is to be served with.\n==See also==\n* [[Gremolata]], similar to persillade but with added lemon zest.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Condiments]]\n[[Category:Herbs]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#persillade #parsley #oliveoil #miseenplace #garlic #breadcrumbs #gremolata #potatoes #panfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pistou sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pistou sauce, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pistousauce #garlic #pesto #oliveoil #sauce #basil #parmesan #basilleaves #cheese #cheeses #herbs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pistou sauce, or just pistou, is a cold sauce made from Cloves of garlic, fresh basil, and olive oil\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 812\n|PortionCalories = 203\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Pistou sauce being made authentically\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Pistou sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A different pesto</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Strange, it tastes very similar</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Pistou sauce''', or just '''pistou''', is a cold [[sauce]] made from Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], fresh [[Basil|basil]], and [[Olive oil|olive oil]]. Some more modern versions of the recipe include [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan|parmesan]], [[Pecorino|pecorino]] or similar hard [[Cheeses|cheeses]]. Traditionally, the ingredients are crushed and mixed together in a mortar with a pestle, (pistou means pounded in the French Proven\u00e7al language). The word \"Pistou\" is an introduction from Genoa dialect \"[[Pesto]]\" as it has been brought in Provence in 19 th century by Italian immigrants from Genoa and Ligury ( 30 % of Provence population are of italian origin).\n===Pistou & Pesto===\nThe key difference between pistou and [[pesto]] is the absence of pinoli ([[Pine nuts|pine nuts]]), from pistou.\n===Pistou: uses===\nIt is a typical [[Condiment|condiment]] from the Provence region of [[France]] and from [[Italian]] regions that can be served with [[Pasta dishes|pasta dishes]] or as a spread for [[Bread|bread]].\n\nIt is most often associated with the Proven\u00e7al dish [[soupe au pistou]] or minestrone al pesto (Ligury)\nBoth pistou and [[Pesto|pesto]] probably share the same origins. The Roman poet Virgil describes a [[Sauce|sauce]] of crushed [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Salt|salt]], and [[Olive oil|olive oil]].  A version with pinoli emerged around Genoa to become pesto, while pistou evolved in the areas around Nice.\n\nSome regions, especially those closer to the Alps, substitute [[Swiss cheese]] in the place of [[Parmesan]]. Whatever [[Cheese|cheese]] is used, it is preferred that it not be a \"stringy\" cheese, so that when it melts in a hot liquid (like in the pistou [[Soup|soup]], for instance) it does not melt into long strands.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| A big handful of fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]]\n| 1 [[Fat|fat]] Clove of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 100ml (4fl oz) [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Blanch]] the [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]] in a pan of [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 5-10 seconds.\n| Drain and rinse under cold water.\n| Drain and carefully press out any excess water.\n| Blitz the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Basil|basil]] in a [[Food processor|food processor]] (using the smallest bowl available).\n| Blend to a pur\u00e9e, adding the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], slowly, a little at a time.\n| Season to taste.\n| [[Refrigerate|Refrigerate]] in a [[Lock and Lock|lock and lock]]-style container until required.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Condiments]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pistousauce #garlic #pesto #oliveoil #sauce #basil #parmesan #basilleaves #cheese #cheeses #herbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo, French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pollocon40dientesdeajo #garlic #chicken #lemon #french #almond #vegetables #miseenplace #mashedpotatoes #roast #ground \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is traditionally French, but has now become part of the cuisine of Spain. The following version is Spanish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 233\n|PortionCalories = 58\n|DatePublished=6th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 to 6 people\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Now that's a lot of garlic!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Delicious!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is traditionally [[French]], but has now become part of the cuisine of [[Spain]].  The following version is [[Spanish]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 60 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Freshly [[Ground|ground]] [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| &frac12; a [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| Several [[Rosemary#Sprigs_of_rosemary|sprigs of fresh rosemary]]\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic|garlic]], cut in half, but not peeled\n| 1 [[Chicken|chicken]] weighing 1.5-2 kg, washed and [[Dried|dried]], [[parson's nose removed]]\n| 4 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], separated into [[Cloves|cloves]], but not peeled\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Place a [[Roasting|roasting]] tin containing the [[Oil|oil]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] in the [[Oven|oven]] and preheat to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8).  \n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Lemon|lemon]] half, [[Rosemary|rosemary]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] halves in the cavity of the [[Chicken|chicken]].\n| Reduce the temperature to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5) and [[Brown|brown]] it for about 5 minutes on each of the three sides.  If you use a rack in your roasting tin, do not use it at this stage.\n| After this stage put the [[chicken]] on its rack (if using) in the oven.\n| Cover the [[Chicken|chicken]] with a double layer of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] and [[Roast|roast]] for 1&frac14;-1&frac34; hours until done.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves after one hour.\n| Remove from [[Oven|oven]] and allow to rest, covered, for about 15 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with the [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves which can be squeezed over the [[Chicken|chicken]].  [[Steamed]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] of your choice and [[Mashed potatoes|mashed potatoes]] would go well with this dish.\n===Variations===\nThere are many variations.  Sometimes, [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces are used and cooked in a pan.  You can use other [[Herbs|herbs]] or replace the [[Oil|oil]] with [[Butter|butter]].  It can be made as a [[Casserole|casserole]], with [[Almond|almond]] slithers.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou do not need to have exactly 40 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]].  It is an estimate only, so just throw in as many as you like.  The [[Garlic|garlic]] will taste sweet and not be at all pungent.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Pollo con 40 dientes de ajo]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pollocon40dientesdeajo #garlic #chicken #lemon #french #almond #vegetables #miseenplace #mashedpotatoes #roast #ground </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Poolish, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#poolish #motherdough #yeast #flour #bread #dough #refrigerate #clingfilm #driedyeast #foodprocessor #ferment \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Poolish is a mother dough made from a mixture of flour and water, sometimes in the same proportions, sometimes with more water, to which no salt is\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 850\n|PortionCalories = 85\n|DatePublished=27th June 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 10 - Makes 1 portion of [[mother dough]]\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 2 days, 4 hours\n |PrepTime = 2 days, 4 hours\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Poolish recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Similar to sourdough starter</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is very similar to the sourdough starters.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nPoolish is a [[Mother dough|mother dough]] made from a mixture of [[Flour|flour]] and water, sometimes in the same proportions, sometimes with more water, to which no [[Salt|salt]] is added.  \nIt can be considered as being a half-way house between natural [[Mother dough|mother doughs]] and and those which use a normal amount of [[Yeast|yeast]], as the proportion of [[yeast]] used is quite low.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 g fresh or 3 g [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]]\n| 320 g strong [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 360 ml water at room temperature\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the ingredients in a bowl or [[Food processor|food processor]] in the order given above and mix until you have a soft, sticky [[Dough|dough]].\n| Cover with [[Cling film|cling film]] and leave for a minimum of 4 and a maximum of 72 hours at room temperature.\n| If you wish to keep it longer, [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nYou may find that you can get away with less [[Yeast|yeast]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe longer you leave the poolish to [[Ferment|ferment]], the better tasting your final [[Bread|bread]] will be.\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Poolish]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Poolish]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Poolish]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian title": "Pork steaks in calvados",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Porksteaks in calvados recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#calvados #marinade #pork #grill #haricotbeans #duckfat #masaharina #oliveoil #griddle #fridge #sauce \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Holidaying in France, we discovered what a marvellous marinade calvados was for pork\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1293\n|PortionCalories = 646\n|DatePublished=19th September 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 5 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Pork steaks in calvados recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">\ud83e\udd69 + \ud83c\udf77 = \ud83e\udd2d</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">\ud83e\udd2d\ud83e\udd2d\ud83e\udd2d</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nWhile on holiday in [[France]] recently we discovered what a marvellous [[Marinade|marinade]] [[Calvados|calvados]] (''apple brandy'') was for [[Pork|pork]] steaks, so once home we tried a sort of [[Tex-Mex|tex-mex]] version to accompany the [[French]] [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]] cooked in [[Duck fat|duck fat]] - very Basque!\n\nTHe meal was fantastic but the presentation could have been improved with a little green, maybe a [[Sweet Pepper|sweet pepper]]?\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 x 160g boneless  [[Pork|pork]] steaks\n| 50 ml (or so) of [[Calvados|calvados]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tex-Mex rub|tex-mex rub]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 6 tablespoon [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] - fine or coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] works almost as well for this\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Tenderise the meat with a [[ Swiss steak|meat tenderiser tool]] if you have one\n* Place the steaks in a [[Lock and Lock box]] together with the [[Calvados|calvados]] and the [[Tex-Mex rub|tex-mex rub]] - \n* Leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for an hour or more if possible shaking now and then to ensure a good cover\n* Preheat the [[Grill|grill]] or [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] - I used a Breville electric grill\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Pork|pork]] steaks and discard the [[Marinade|marinade]] - it could be used for making a [[Sauce|sauce]] but I didn't need gravy this time\n| Add the [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] to a large place and press the steaks into the [[Flour|flour]] to coat\n| [[Oil]] the [[Grill|grill]] with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Griddle|griddle]] for about 8 minutes - turning once if not using a double-sided griddle\n| Leave to [[Rest for|rest for]] 5 minutes\n| Serve\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Masa grilled pork steaks.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Steaks griddled in masa harina, ready to rest\nImage:Pork marinading in calvados.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinating in calvados\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe had this with Basque [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]] in [[Duck fat|duck fat]] - very healthy!\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#calvados #marinade #pork #grill #haricotbeans #duckfat #masaharina #oliveoil #griddle #fridge #sauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [
                    {
