                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Potage bonne femme (Leek and potato soup) a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#butter #vegetables #leeks #potato #soup #onion #leek #potatoes #chickenstock #vegetable #boiling \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Leek and potato soup which is popular throughout France\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1632\n|PortionCalories = 408\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Vichyssoise.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely leeks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is fab if you grow them</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Leek]] and [[Potato|potato]] [[Soup|soup]] which is popular throughout France.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 medium [[Leeks|leeks]], dark green leaves removed and sliced\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 [[Clove garlic, crushed|clove garlic, crushed]]\n| 50 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 250 g [[Potatoes|potatoes]], sliced \n| 1 pint [[Vegetable|vegetable]] or light [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| Seasoning\n| 560 ml [[Milk|milk]] or less\n| 140 ml [[Single cream|single cream]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Melt the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan and slowly [[Stew|stew]] (covered) the [[Leeks|leeks]], [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until they are soft - around 10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Stock|stock]] and seasoning.\n| When the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are cooked, remove a few [[Leek|leek]] slices and [[Potato|potato]], reserve, and pur\u00e9e the rest.\n| Return the pur\u00e9ed [[Soup|soup]] to the pan and add the [[Milk|milk]] until you have the consistency you require.\n| Add the [[Cream|cream]], and reserved [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and reheat without [[Boiling|boiling]].\n| Garnish with cro\u00fbtons if desired.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with slices of fresh [[Baguette|baguette]].\n===Variations===\n[[Vichyssoise]] is a chilled version of Potage bonne femme and uses [[oil]] rather than [[butter]] (which would solidify).\n--[[User:JuliaBalbilla|JuliaBalbilla]] 19:36, 10 February 2009 (UTC)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:Starters|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Leek and potato soup]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #vegetables #leeks #potato #soup #onion #leek #potatoes #chickenstock #vegetable #boiling </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Really love the olives.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}} \nA nice Mediterranean-style [[Chicken|chicken]] recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.6kg oven ready [[Chicken|chicken]] \n| 2 sprigs fresh [[Marjoram|marjoram]], leaves only \n| A good handful of [[Thyme|thyme]], leaves only \n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] \n| 5 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n| 1 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]], sliced thinly - (flesh discarded)\n| 175g [[Belazu]] [[Black olives|black olives]] with [[Herbs]], stoned \n| 250g [[Button mushrooms|button mushrooms]]\n| 1 green [[sweet pepper]], de-seeded and sliced\n| 40g sun-[[Dried|dried]] or sun-blush [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], soaked in hot water and drained\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], sliced\n| 1 fresh [[bay leaf]]\n| 175ml [[Dry white wine|dry white wine]]\n| [[Sea salt]] & [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pot Roasted Mediterranean Chicken carved.jpg|Carving Pot Roasted Mediterranean Chicken\nImage:Pot Roasted Mediterranean Chicken, cooked.jpg|Pot Roasted Mediterranean Chicken, cooked\nImage:Pot Roasted Mediterranean Chicken.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Garlic and herb rubbed.jpg|Garlic, [[olive oil]] and [[herb]] rub, the lazy way\nImage:Garlic and herb rub.jpg|Garlic and [[herb]] rub.  I added a some [[parsley]] to bulk out my meagre winter herbs\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]] from the chicken.\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] inside and out. [[Mash]] the [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] with 3 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]] to form a paste.\n| Slide your fingers between the skin and flesh of the [[Chicken|chicken]] and rub the paste as evenly as possible over the breasts. Chop half of the [[Lemon slices|lemon slices]] and mix with half the [[Olives|olives]] and half the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]]. Stuff the cavity with this mixture. in the cavity. \n| Put the bird in a heavy [[Casserole|casserole]] (such as [[Le Creuset]]). Scatter round the [[Sun-dried tomatoes|sun-dried tomatoes]], [[green pepper]] slices, [[Onion|onion]], remaining [[Lemon|lemon]], [[olives]] and [[mushrooms]] and pour over the [[Wine|wine]] and the remaining olive oil.\n| [[Roast]] for about 1 &frac34; hours.  Covered for the first 45 minutes, remove the cover then [[Baste|baste]] every 20 minutes until the chicken is properly cooked,\n| To serve, spoon the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] from the cavity and set the [[Chicken|chicken]] on a board. \n| Skim [[Fat|fat]] off the juices in the [[Casserole|casserole]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and serve hot with the carved chicken. Delicious with [[barley couscous]].\n}}\n''(Orlando Murrin in The Daily Express)''\n\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nDelicious with [[barley couscous]].\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/black-with-herbs.html Belazu black herb olives]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/traditional-barley-couscous.html Belazu Traditional Barley Couscous]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potroastedmediterraneanchicken #chicken #barleycouscous #herb #belazu #oliveoil #onion #mushrooms #herbs #garlic #olives </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [

[[Poule au pot (for 4)|The version for 4 people is here]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.2 kg corn fed [[chicken]], giblets removed\n| 1 large [[Leek|leek]], washed, trimmed and sliced\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and cut into eight pieces\n| 3 small [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 handful fresh [[Parsley|parsley]], chopped\n| 1 teaspoon of fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]] leaves, chopped or 1 teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] tarragon\n| 3 sticks of [[Celery|celery]], peeled and chopped roughly\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n| 1 small whole bulb of garlic, unpeeled\n| 10 whole [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 2 baking sized [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into eight pieces\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]] from the chicken.\n| Rinse the chicken under cold running water and pat it dry\n| Find a pot that the [[Chicken|chicken]] will just fit into.\n| Add all of the ingredients apart from the [[Potatoes|potatoes]]\n| Put the [[Chicken|chicken]] on top then just cover with [[Boiling|boiling]] water\n| Bring back to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 50 minutes\n| After 50 minutes, add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and cook until a knife easily pierces the potatoes\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Poule au pot recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right\nImage:Poule au pot ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice and serve with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]], crusty bread, some of the [[Stock|stock]] and a big dollop of [[Garlic mayonnaise|garlic mayonnaise]], or, if you any, some leftover [[\u00e7a\u00e7iki]].\n===Chef's notes===\nHaving made this, I have discovered another fairly obvious benefit of making this.  Really good chicken stock.  You probably wont use all of the vegetables and original stock. Just chuck the chicken carcass back into the pot with a little water and a few more vegetables if you have any laying around.  Boil up and simmer for 15 to 20 minutes, allow to cool and then strain and freeze.  I got more than a litre of good chicken stock from this.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #potatoes #vegetables #stewedbraisedorpotroasted #simmer #onion #boil #carrots #celery #bayleaf #potroasted </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Winner!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAn economical, yet tasty take on the famous [[Lobster thermidor]] recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1lb) cooked [[King prawns|king prawns]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 3 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]]\n| 3 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 275 ml (1/2 pint) full [[Cream|cream]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 5 tablespoons (60  ml) [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| pinch of [[Salt|salt]] - not too much [[parmesan]] can be quite salty\n| 1/3 teaspoon of [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]] (not [[Smoked|smoked]])\n| 1/3 teaspoon of [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]]\n| 80 g freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]]\n| grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Grill|grill]].\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Ensure the [[Prawns|prawns]] are properly [[defrosted]] if [[Frozen|frozen]].\n| Pat the [[Prawns|prawns]] dry on a [[tea-towel]].\n| melt half of the [[Butter|butter]] in a pan and gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] until translucent.\n| Add the [[Flour|flour]], mix into a [[Roux|roux]] and then gradually stir in the [[milk]].\n| Just start to bring the sauce to the boil then reduce the heat and stir until it thickens.\n| Add the [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Tarragon|tarragon]].\n| Mix in the [[Sherry|sherry]] and [[Spices|spices]], season to taste and adjust to your liking.\n| Add the [[Prawns|prawns]], remaining [[Butter|butter]] and half of the [[Cheese|cheese]].  Mix well and then spoon the mixture into lightly greased gratin dishes.\n| Sprinkle with the remaining [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Brown|brown]] under the [[Grill|grill]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse normal [[Peeled prawns|peeled prawns]] instead of the large [[King prawns|king prawns]]\n\nUse [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]]\n\nAdd lots of Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] with the [[Onions|onions]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf using raw prawns, cook them with the [[Onions|onions]] until they turn pink and remove them while you make the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n\nIf you are struggling to get hold of fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]], at  a push you could add 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Dried|dried]] tarragon to a little [[Boiled|boiled]] water, allow it to rehydrate, drain any liquid and then use, however, fresh is plainly better.\n\nThis was very delicious and will be made again and again.\n==See also==\n{{Template:Lobster recipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#prawns #tarragon #prawnthermidor #butter #onions #kingprawns #grill #cheese #parsley #roux #lobsterthermidor </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Perhaps this picture will remind me next time!]]\nQuiche Lorraine is perhaps the most common variety of quiche. In addition to the eggs and cream, it includes bacon or lardons.  I know cheese is not really an ingredient of a true Quiche Lorraine, but rather than use double cream, I prefer to use [[mascarpone cheese]] or [[ricotta cheese]], both or more like cream than [[cheese]] and work really well in a savoury flan.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 157 g (6 oz) -half a block of ready-made [[shortcrust pastry]]\n| 3 [[free range eggs]], beaten\n| 45 ml (4 tablespoons) of [[milk]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[mascarpone cheese]] or [[ricotta cheese]]\n| 5 rashers of cooked [[bacon]], [[home smoked bacon]] or [[ham]], chopped into tiny pieces.\n| [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Slices of [[tomato]] or [[red pepper]] or [[green pepper]] or a mixture of all to garnish\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - Gas 6)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roll the pastry and use it to line a greased 20 cm (8\") [[push-out flan dish]]\n| [[Blind baking|Bake blind]] at 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - Gas 6) for 10 minutes\n| Beat the [[eggs]], [[milk]], [[mascarpone cheese]] and season to taste with [[pepper]] -  [[salt]] won't be needed with the bacon\n| Stir in the bacon pieces\n| Pour the egg and bacon mixture into the blind-baked flan case\n| Decorate with whatever you have to hand, I used half of a [[green pepper]], sliced, but use whatever you have to hand, [[tomatoes]] look and taste good.\n| Reduce the heat of the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4)\n| [[Bake]] for a further 40 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot or cold\n\n{{Quiche - See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#quichelorraine #mascarponecheese #bacon #ricottacheese #greenpepper #bake #cheese #greaseproofpaper #freerangeeggs #redpepper #homesmokedbacon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

A nice meal for a hot summers evening that would also work as a starter or meze.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 5 large ripe [[Apricots|apricots]]\n| Zest and juice of half a [[lemon]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[honey]] - '''Tip:''' Microwave ''set'' honey for 5 seconds to make it runny\n| 10g of [[butter]]\n| 20 pistachio nuts\n| 100g [[goats cheese|goat's cheese]]\n| 2 slices of orange\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* As most supermarkets seem to sell [[Fruit|fruit]] that is as hard as bullets, it might be an idea to buy your fruit ahead of time to allow them to ripen properly first.\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Separate the [[Apricots|apricots]] by cutting round the middle and twisting the two halves apart. Remove any stubborn left-over bits with a sharp knife.\n| Wipe the base of a small [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] with [[Butter|butter]] paper or [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| Sit the [[Apricots|apricots]] in the tray so they are an array of ''cups''.\n| fill each ''[[Cup|cup]]'' with a dot of [[Butter|butter]], half a teaspoon of [[Honey|honey]], a squeeze of [[Lemon|lemon]] and a pinch of [[Salt|salt]].\n| [[Roast]] for 15 minutes or until the [[Fruit|fruit]] is gooey and runny.\n| After 15 minutes, add a teaspoon of [[Goat|goat]]'s [[Cheese|cheese]] to each [[Apricot|apricot]] and [[Roast|roast]] for a further 5 minutes to soften the cheese.\n| Shell the [[Pistachios|pistachios]], pop them in a clean [[Tea-towel|tea-towel]] and smash them to crumbs with a [[Rolling pin|rolling pin]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the warm [[Apricots|apricots]] on a bed of [[Rocket|rocket]], lightly dressed with [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n\nSprinkle with crushed [[Pistachios|pistachios]] and dress with [[Orange|orange]] slices.\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Lindsey Bareham, The Times newspaper, Thursday 15th June 2017\n===Variations===\nTry this with [[Roquefort|roquefort]] blue in place of the [[Goat|goat]]'s [[Cheese|cheese]] might be nice too?\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French title": "Roux",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=What is a roux (cookery term) Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#roux #flour #fat #clarifiedbutter #wheatflour #butter #sauceespagnole #vegetableoils #sauces #lard #vegetableoil \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Roux is a mixture of wheat flour and fat and is the basis for many well known sauces\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Frying butter and flour.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Frying the butter and flour to make a roux|alt=Roux cookery term sauce making]]\n==What is a roux? (cooking term)==\n\nRoux (pronounced somewhat like the English word \"rue\") is a mixture of [[wheat flour]] and [[fat]]. It is the basis of three of the mother sauces of classical French cooking: [[sauce b\u00e9chamel]], [[sauce velout\u00e9]], and [[sauce espagnole]]. [[Butter]], [[vegetable oils]], or [[lard]] are common fats used. It is used as a base for gravy, other sauces, souffl\u00e9s, [[:Category:Soup and stock recipes|soups and stews]].\n\nThe [[fat]] is heated in a pot or pan melting it if necessary, then the [[flour]] is added. The mixture is stirred until the [[flour]] is incorporated and then cooked until at least the point where a raw flour taste is no longer apparent or until desired colour has been reached. The final results can range from the nearly white to the nearly black, depending on the length of time it is over the heat, and its intended use. The end result is a thickening and flavouring agent.\n\nRoux is most often made with butter as the [[fat]] base but it may be made with any edible fat. In the case of meat gravies, they are often made with rendered fat from the meat. In regional American cuisine, bacon is sometimes fried to produce fat to use in the roux. [[Vegetable oil]] is often used when producing dark roux as it does not burn at high temperatures like [[butter]] will.\n\nWhen combining roux with water-based liquids, such as soup or [[milk]], it is important that these liquids are not excessively hot. It is preferable to add room temperature or warm liquid into a moderately hot or warm roux. They should be added in small quantities to the roux while stirring, to ensure proper mixing. Otherwise, the mixture will be very lumpy, not homogeneous, and not properly thickened.\n\nCooks can cheat by adding a mixture of water and [[wheat flour]] to a dish which needs thickening since the heat of boiling water will release the starch from the flour, however this temperature is not high enough to eliminate the floury taste. A mixture of water and flour used in this way is colloquially known as cowboy roux since it imparts a flavour to the finished dish which a traditional haute cuisine chef would consider unacceptable.\n\n==Types of roux==\nIn classic French cuisine there are three types of roux:\n\n'''Brown roux''' is used to thicken [[sauces]] such as [[Sauce espagnole|Espagnole]].  It is traditionally made in the oven with equal amount of [[clarified butter]] and [[flour]] and is cooked gently in the oven for a long time, stirring frequently.  Nowadays it is usually made in a saucepan on the hob over a low heat for about 10 minutes.  It can also be made with clarified [[fat]] from a 'petite marmite'.  It should be of a good light brown colour and keeps fairly well.\n\n'''Blond roux''' is made only with equal quantities of [[clarified butter]] and [[flour]] and is cooked more quickly than '''brown roux'''.  It is only made as when needed and should be pale gold in colour.\n\n'''White roux''' is used for [[B\u00e9chamel sauce| B\u00e9chamel]] and [[Sauce velout\u00e9|Velout\u00e9]] sauces and special thick soups.  Equal quantities of [[clarified butter]] and [[flour]] are cooked over heat for 5 minutes, constantly stirred with a wooden spoon.\n{{Template:WhatLinksHere}}\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Roux]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#roux #flour #fat #clarifiedbutter #wheatflour #butter #sauceespagnole #vegetableoils #sauces #lard #vegetableoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

title": "Sauce espagnole",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sauce espagnole, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sauce #sauceespagnole #butter #stock #flour #tomatoes #mushrooms #ham #carrot #celery #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=In cooking, espagnole sauce is one of the mother sauces that are the basis of sauce-making in classic French cooking\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 924\n|PortionCalories = 51\n|DatePublished=28th February 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 18 - Makes about 600ml\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 3 hours 55 minutes\n|PrepTime = 25 minutes\n|CookTime = 3 hours 30 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:Sauce espagnole.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">This is proper gravy!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not your Bisto granules, NO. Proper gravy - well worth the effoert.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nIn cooking, espagnole [[sauce]] is one of the mother [[sauces]] that are the basis of sauce-making in classic French cooking. Auguste Escoffier codified the recipe in the late 19th century, which is still followed today.\n\nEven though espagnole is the French word for Spanish, the sauce has little connection with Spanish cuisine. According to Louis Diat, the creator of [[vichyssoise]] and the author of the classic Gourmet's Basic French Cookbook: \"There is a story that explains why the most important basic brown [[sauce]] in French cuisine is called sauce espagnole, or Spanish sauce. According to the story, the Spanish cooks of Louis XIII's bride, Anne, helped to prepare their wedding feast, and insisted upon improving the rich brown [[sauce]] of France with Spanish [[tomatoes]]. This new sauce was an instant success, and was gratefully named in honour of its creators.\"\n\nEspagnole has a strong taste and is rarely used directly on food. As a mother [[sauce]], however, it then serves as the starting point for many derivative sauces, such as Sauce Africaine, Sauce Bigarade, Sauce Bourguignonne, Sauce aux Champignons, Sauce Charcutiere, Sauce Chasseur, Sauce Chevreuil and Demi-glace. There are hundreds of other derivatives in the classic French repertoire.\n\nA typical espagnole recipe takes many hours or even several days to make, and produces four to five quarts of sauce. In most derivative recipes, however, one cup of espagnole is more than enough, so that the basic recipe will yield enough [[sauce]] for 16 to 20 meals. [[Frozen]] in small quantities, espagnole will keep practically indefinitely.  The following recipe is for a much smaller quantity.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 25g unsalted [[butter]]\n| 1 tbsp [[ham]], finely diced\n| 1 large [[carrot]], peeled and diced\n| 1 [[onion]], finely chopped\n| 1 stick [[celery]], finely chopped\n| 2 tbsps [[mushrooms]], chopped\n| 1 [[bay leaf]]\n| 1 sprig [[thyme]]\n| 25g plain [[flour]]\n| 1 litre strong [[meat]] [[stock]], heated\n| 600g tinned, chopped [[tomatoes]] or use the equivalent in fresh if they are ripe enough\n| Seasoning\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Melt half of the [[butter]] in a heavy pan.\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[ham]], [[carrot]], [[onion]], [[celery]], [[mushrooms]] and the [[herbs]] for about 20-30 minutes until they are soft and slightly caramelised.\n| Remove from the pan and reserve.\n| Melt the remaining [[butter]], add the [[flour]] and stir until the mixture becomes nut brown.\n| Remove from the heat and stir in a little [[stock]].\n| Return the [[flour]] mixture to the heat and gradually stir in the remaining [[stock]] until smooth.\n| Bring to the boil, add the reserved [[vegetables]] and the [[tomatoes]]. \n| Bring to the boil again and reduce the heat.\n| Simmer (it should not bubble) very gently for 2-3 hours until the [[sauce]] has reduced by half.\n| Skim from time to time.\n| Allow to cool slightly, then strain through muslin.\n| Put a few small pieces of [[butter]] over the top to prevent a skin forming.\n}}\n\n===Variations===\nThere are some derivative recipes which call for this to be [[fish]] based, in which case substitute the [[meat]] [[stock]] for [[fish]] stock.\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sauce #sauceespagnole #butter #stock #flour #tomatoes #mushrooms #ham #carrot #celery #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

title": "Sauce hongroise",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Slice the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] as thinly as you can with a [[Mandolin|mandolin]], if you have one.\n| Grease a shallow [[Baking|baking]] dish with a little of the [[Butter|butter]].\n| Part-[[Bake|bake]] your [[Sausages|sausages]] in a lightly oiled [[Baking tray|baking tray]] in the preheated [[Oven|oven]] for 15 minutes, shaking the pan once or twice during that time.\n| Remove and put to one side.\n| When cool enough to handle, slice the sausages in half lengthways.\n| Melt the remaining [[Butter|butter]] along with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Sweat|sweat]] gently for 10 minutes.\n| Now layer the [[Potato|potato]] slices, [[Sausage|sausage]] pieces and the [[Onion|onion]] mix in the greased dish, seasoning as you go.\n| Pour the [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] over the whole dish so that the contents are only just covered. Don't use all the [[Stock|stock]] if you don't need to.\n| Now cover the dish with [[Foil|foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] in the preheated [[Oven|oven]] for 30 minutes.\n| Remove the foil and cook for another 30 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe this one pot meal immediately.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #butter #onions #potatoes #bake #sausages #chickenstock #glutenfree #oliveoil #miseenplace #stock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe fills the aubergines with a [[Sausagemeat|sausagemeat]] [[Stuffing|stuffing]].\n\nIt is also suitable for coeliacs as it uses [[Gluten free|gluten free]] ingredients.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 [[Aubergine|aubergine]], halved lengthways\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 125ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 pack [[Debbie and Andrew's Harrogate 97% Gluten Free Pork Sausages]]\n| 2 cloves of [[garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons of chopped fresh [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 125ml [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 240g fresh [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] (make with [[Gluten free|gluten free]] [[Bread|bread]], if required)\n| 50g [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove all the [[Sausages|sausages]] from their skins. Put to one side in a large bowl.\n| [[Scoop]] out the flesh of the [[Aubergine|aubergine]], then chop it and place it in a [[Sieve|sieve]] over the sink. Sprinkle with a little [[Salt|salt]] and leave to drain.\n| Season the [[Aubergine|aubergine]] skins with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Brush|brush]] with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]]. Set to one side.\n| Now heat 4 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]]. Cook the [[Sausage meat|sausage meat]] with the [[Garlic|garlic]] until [[Browned|browned]]. Break up the [[Meat|meat]] as much as you can as you cook.\n| Squeeze as much moisture as you can from the [[Aubergine|aubergine]] and add to the pan.\n| Add the [[Parsley|parsley]] and plenty of seasoning.\n| Pour in the [[Wine|wine]] and cook for 5 minutes.\n| Now remove from the heat and add the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and half the [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]].\n| Stuff this mixture into the [[Aubergine|aubergine]] skins and sprinkle the tops with the remaining [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] in the preheated [[Oven|oven]] for 30 minutes until tender and golden.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately with a spicy [[Rocket|rocket]] or [[Watercress|watercress]] [[Salad|salad]].\n==See also==\n\n* [[Udi\u0092s Gluten Free Products]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#aubergine #oliveoil #parmesancheese #glutenfree #sausagemeat #parsley #garlic #breadcrumbs #scoop #salad #brush </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Small baguettes",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Small baguettes, French recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#dough #flour #clingfilm #yeast #smallbaguettes #knead #bread #baguettes #bake #sieve #kneading \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=My first attempt at these! This is based on a recipe in Richard Bertinet's book 'Dough'\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1329\n|PortionCalories = 332\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 8 hours, 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 8 hours\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Small baguettes recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">  <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hard Work!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.74</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But worth all the effort for the authentic taste.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nMy first attempt at these!  This is based on a recipe in  Richard Berthinet's '''[[Dough]]''' (ISBN 9781856267625).  I have started by making an overnight sponge, to encourage [[Yeast|yeast]] activity, but you can omit that stage if you like and mix in all the ingredients at the same time.\n\nThis time, I am letting my Kenwood Chef do a lot of the hard work.  If using a stand food [[Mixer|mixer]], you can use its bowl right from starting the sponge.  For a Kenwood Chef, you can use the bowl cover that comes with it, rather than mess about with [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]].   I am not sure if Kitchen Aids come with a clip on cover, so if they don't you will have to remove the bowl from the machine and cover with clingfilm or a damp cloth.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 10g fresh [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 350g [[Sparkling mineral water|sparkling mineral water]]\n| 500g strong [[Bread|bread]] [[Flour|flour]] - you may need to use more water if using very strong bread [[Flour|flour]]\n| 10g [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| The night before you want to [[Bake|bake]] the [[Bread|bread]], dissolve the [[Yeast|yeast]] in the water,\n| [[Sieve]] 250g [[Flour|flour]] into a large bowl and stir in the water and dissolved [[Yeast|yeast]]. Do NOT add the [[Salt|salt]] at this stage as its will interfere with yeast activity.\n| Mix thoroughly.\n| Cover with [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]] and leave at room temperature overnight.\n| If it becomes very active, [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] and bring to room temperature in the morning.\n| The next day, [[Sieve|sieve]] the remaining 250g [[Flour|flour]] with the [[Salt|salt]] and add to the bowl.\n| Mix thoroughly (Kenwood Chef - lowest speed for 2 minutes) and leave to rest for 20 minutes. The [[Dough|dough]] should be fairly sticky, so add more water if necessary. \n| [[Knead]], using your desired method until you have an elastic [[Dough|dough]]  (Kenwood - 2nd slowest speed for 6 minutes).\n| Shape into a ball and leave it to rest for an hour in an oiled bowl, covered with [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]], until the [[Dough|dough]] has almost doubled in size.\n| Lightly [[Flour|flour]] a work surface and gently deflate the [[Dough|dough]].  (Kenwood - deflate for a few seconds on slowest speed - no need for further [[Kneading|kneading]].)\n| [[Knead]] briefly and repeat the two previous steps, but do not vigorously deflate the [[Dough|dough]].\n| Divide into 4 equal pieces and allow to rest, covered, on the work surface.\n| Shape each piece into [[Baguettes|baguettes]] and place on a floured couche cloth or [[Baguette|baguette]] tin.\n| Cover and leave to prove for about 45 minutes until almost doubled in size.\n| Cover with a damp cloth or oiled [[Clingfilm|clingfilm]] and leave to prove for up to 45 minutes.\n| Make a few diagonal slashes in the loaves and leave to rest for a further 10 minutes\n| [[Bake]] at 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 210\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour] for 15 minutes.\n| Allow to cool on a wire rack.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nI am still trying to get the knack of slashing the [[Dough|dough]]!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #flour #clingfilm #yeast #smallbaguettes #knead #bread #baguettes #bake #sieve #kneading </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sous vide spatchcock chicken with bulb fennel orange and onion recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#orange #sousvidespatchcockchickenwithbulbfennelorangeandonion #onion #chicken #zest #sousvidecooking #sousvidebath #fennelbulb #fennel #gravy #liquor \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I thought I would make a sous vide version of one of my favourite recipes; Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2598\n|PortionCalories = 1299\n|DatePublished=21st February 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  8 hours, 20 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Sous vide spatchcock chicken with bulb fennel orange and onion recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Rubbish!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Don't waste your time making this!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:WorkInProgress}}\nI thought I would make a [[Sous Vide|sous vide]] version of one of my favourite recipes; [[Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions]].  I've used an [[Orange|orange]] instead of a [[Lemon|lemon]]. As [[Sous vide cooking|sous vide cooking]] tends to intensify the flavours I removed all of the [[Bitter|bitter]] pith by cutting off with the rind and just including a few strips of [[Lemon zest|lemon zest]].\n\n===Not as good as expected===\nThis was inferior to the [[Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions|roast version]].  I felt it was overcooked with a mushy mouthfeel. It was still nice, but not worth all the extra effort.\n\nI will redo shortly, leaving the skin on, adding garlic butter and without peeling the orange.  We'll get there in the end!\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.5kg (medium-sized) whole [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| 1 [[Fennel bulb|fennel bulb]], chopped\n| 1 small [[Brown|brown]] [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 1 whole [[Orange|orange]]\n| A pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Sous vide bath|sous vide bath]] to 71\u00b0C (''159.8\u00b0F'')\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Sous vide spatchcock chicken with bulb fennel orange and onion cooked.jpg|Cooked chicken breasts removed, ready to plate up\nImage:Sous vide spatchcock chicken with bulb fennel orange and onion bagged.jpg|Vacuum packed and ready to cook\nImage:Sous vide spatchcock chicken with bulb fennel orange and onion.jpg|Spatchcocked and skinned with the basic ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove the [[Parson's nose|parson's nose]] and [[Spatchcock|spatchcock]] the [[Chicken|chicken]], skin the chicken and trim and discard as much [[Fat|fat]] as you can.  I've also snipped the wing-tips and removed any obvious stray [[bones]].\n| Season with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] and drop into a suitable sized [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] bag.  My widest bag, cut to 30cm [12\"] was plenty large enough.\n| Remove the core from the [[Fennel bulb|fennel bulb]] and roughly chop.\n| Peel and roughly chop the [[Onion|onion]].\n| Reserve a few strips of [[Zest|zest]] from the [[Orange|orange]], then use a knife to remove the pith and skin. Discard.\n| Quarter the [[Orange|orange]] and add to the bag, together with the [[Zest|zest]], chopped [[Fennel|fennel]] and [[Onion|onion]].\n| [[Vacuum seal]] and cook in a [[Sous vide bath|sous vide bath]] at 71\u00b0C (''159.8\u00b0F'') for 8 hours.\n| I tend to discard the [[Orange|orange]], most of the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Fennel|fennel]], using the remnants and the cooking [[Liquor|liquor]] to flavour the [[Gravy|gravy]]. [[Chicken]] gravy granules is a good [[Cheat|cheat]] for the gravy!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]] and a [[Green vegetable|green vegetable]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Based in [[Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#orange #sousvidespatchcockchickenwithbulbfennelorangeandonion #onion #chicken #zest #sousvidecooking #sousvidebath #fennelbulb #fennel #gravy #liquor </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#spatchcockedchickenwithfennelandonions #fennel #chicken #lemon #roast #onions #oliveoil #baste #blackpepper #gravy #roastingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Spatchcocking is a different way to prepare a bird and is very easy with a pair of poultry shears\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 223\n|PortionCalories = 55\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Much easier than it looks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I thought this would be difficult but it's actually rather easy to do.  The results look and taste impressive./</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Spatchcocking]] is a different way to prepare a bird and is very easy with a pair of [[poultry shears]].  In this recipe it results in a crispy flavourful bird.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 medium-sized [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Parson's nose|parson's nose removed]]\n| 1 [[Lemon|lemon]], bruised and halved\n| 8 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], 4 peeled and crushed, 4 peeled, bashed and left whole\n| 1 large [[onion|onion]]\n| [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and freshly [[Ground|ground]] back [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[plain flour]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Spatchcocked chicken, oven ready.jpg|Spatchcock chicken, ready for the oven\nImage:Spatchcocked chicken garlic rub.jpg|Rub the garlic/lemon oil over the bird\nImage:Spatchcock chicken fennel and onion bed.jpg|A bed of fennel, onions, garlic and lemon\nImage:Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions_ingredients.jpg|Spatchcocked chicken with fennel and onions, the ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Spatchcock]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] - [[Spatchcock|see here for details]]\n| Find a [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] that is large enough to take the bird laid out flat\n| Peel and slice the [[Onions|onions]]\n| Slice the [[Fennel|fennel]] and roughly chop any green leaves\n| [[Oil]] the tray and layer the base with the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Fennel|fennel]]\n| Add the juice of the [[Lemon|lemon]] to the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]], a glug of olive oil and a generous seasoning of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and rub this all over the bird\n| Lay the bird, skin-side-up in the tray and tuck the whole [[Garlic|garlic]] [[Cloves|cloves]] and [[Fennel|fennel]] leaves anywhere you can\n| Drizzle a little more [[olive oil]] over the bird, garnish with a final grind of [[black pepper]], cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]], seal and [[Roast|roast]] for 30 minutes\n| Remove the [[Foil|foil]], [[Baste|baste]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] and [[Roast|roast]] uncovered for a further 30 to 45 minutes.\n| Remove the chicken to a warm plate and cover with foil\n| Heat the roasting tray on the hob, sprinkle 2 tablespoons of flour into the cooking juices and mix well to make delicious [[gravy]].  Heat until it thickens then serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nAlmost anything would go with this.  [[Tex-Mex potato wedges]] and [[broccoli]] worked for us!\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are not eating this in one sitting, store the remaining meat in a large [[Lock and Lock]] style box and refrigerate one cooled. This way you will have moist chicken the next day, not dried-out meat.\n==See also==\n* [[Spatchcock|How to spatchcock a chicken, step-by-step pictures]]\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spatchcock\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spatchcockedchickenwithfennelandonions #fennel #chicken #lemon #roast #onions #oliveoil #baste #blackpepper #gravy #roastingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Stuffed cabbage leaves",

It is a [[French]] recipe, typical of the Lorraine region.\n[[Image:Cheese and tomato sauce added, ready for the oven.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cheese and tomato sauce added, ready for the oven]]\n[[Image:Finished mince with two baby cabbages.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Finished mince with two baby cabbages]]\n\nIt was nice but the stems of the cabbage were rather tough so when I next make it I will use 1 large cabbage and make two `leaves` from each one by cutting in half and discarding the stem.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 freshly picked [[Cabbage|cabbage]]\n| 500 g (1 lb) lean [[Sausage|sausage]] [[Meat|meat]]\n| 1 thick slice of stale [[White bread|white bread]] soaked in little [[Milk|milk]] for 30 minutes to soften.\n|* If using dried breadcrumbs, allow 1 cup with 120 ml of milk\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| A handful of freshly picked mixed [[Herbs|herbs]] - [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Thyme|thyme]], [[Rosemary|rosemary]], etc. stems removed and finely chopped.\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| About a tablespoon of [[Butter]]\n| 100 g Gruy\u00e8re [[Cheese|cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Clean and trim the [[Cabbage|cabbage]], removing any woody parts.\n| [[Blanch]] the [[Cabbage|cabbage]] in salted [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 15 minute. Remove and drain, reserving the cooking liquor.\n| Cook the [[Sausage|sausage]]-[[Meat|meat]] in 5 or 6 tablespoons of the [[Cabbage|cabbage]] liquor for about 15 minutes, breaking it up now and then.  When the meat has cooked for 15 minutes, remove and drain, reserving the cooking juices to add to the tomato pur\u00e9e.\n| Squeeze most of the milk from the bread and break into small pieces.\n| Mix the [[Garlic|garlic]], cooked sausage meat, bread and [[Herbs|herbs]] together and season well.\n| Remove the leaves, cutting out any really hard stalks and add 1 tablespoon of the [[Sausage|sausage]]-[[Meat|meat]] to each leaf and roll into an oval.\n| Mix the [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e with about 284 ml (1/2 pint) of the cooking liquor.\n| Pack the rolled leaves into an [[Oven|oven]]-proof dish and pour the tomato sauce over the top.\n| Place a few dabs of [[Butter|butter]] over the [[Cabbage|cabbage]] and sprinkle with the [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| Add another grind of pepper and [[Bake]] for 25 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Jacket potatoes|jacket potatoes]] or [[Mashed potatoes|mashed potatoes]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\nRather than buy dubious [[sausage meat]], I used a 250 g of [[pork fillet]] (blitzed in a [[food processor]] with a metal blade) and 250 g [[minced]] [[beef]].  I also added a little fat from my [[Home smoked bacon]].\n\n2 baby [[cabbages]] and were just enough.  When cooking them, half cover them with water, boil with a lid and turn them often.\n\nI added a glug of white wine to the tomato sauce as there was some in the fridge.\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Minced beef and pork tenderloin.jpg|Minced beef and pork tenderloin\nImage:Finished mince with two baby cabbages.jpg|Finished mince with two baby cabbages\nImage:Tomato sauce.jpg|Ready to construct\nImage:A tablespoon in every cabbage leaf.jpg|A tablespoon in every cabbage leaf\nImage:All rolled up.jpg|All rolled up\nImage:Cheese and tomato sauce added, ready for the oven.jpg|Cheese and tomato sauce added, ready for the oven\nImage:Stuffed cabbage leaves recipe.jpg|Stuffed cabbage leaves\n</gallery>\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#stuffedcabbageleaves #cabbage #sausage #cheese #herbs #garlic #grated #tomato #butter #rosemary #beef </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is spread on [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Bread|bread]] and used as an [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to all sorts of dishes.\n===Variations===\nThere is a variation of this recipe which has more ingredients:  2 tbsps [[Sherry vinegar]] and aromatic [[Herbs|herbs]] to taste.  \n\nIn this case the [[Anchovies|anchovies]] are omitted.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#anchovies #blend #capers #thermomix #garlic #blackpepper #bread #sherryvinegar #toasted #blackolives #herbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Yummy \ud83d\ude0d</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]])</span></span>\n}}\nThis is a [[French]] [[Pear|pear]] and [[Almond|almond]] tart which was first created by a [[Pastry|pastry]] chef of the Rue Bourdaloue in Paris\n{{RecipeIngredients\n}}\n====For the [[Pastry]]====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200g [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 100g [[Unsalted butter|unsalted butter]]\n| 50g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]]\n}}\n====For the Stock Syrup====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 500ml water\n| 150g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| The [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 2 [[Pears|pears]], peeled and cored, but left whole\n}}\n====For the Almond Cream====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 100g [[Unsalted butter|unsalted butter]]\n| 100g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| 100g [[Ground almonds|ground almonds]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| 10g [[Flour|flour]]\n| 1tsp [[Almond extract|almond extract]]\n}}\n====To finish====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 50g Hot [[Apricot|apricot]] [[Jam|jam]] (sieved)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n====For the [[Pastry]]==== \n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rub the [[Butter|butter]] into the [[Flour|flour]] to form breadcrumbs\u0092.\n| Mix the [[Egg|egg]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] together in a separate bowl and add to the [[Flour|flour]] and [[Butter|butter]].\n| Mix to form a [[Dough|dough]], wrap in [[Foil|foil]] or [[Cling Film|cling film]], then [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]].\n}}\n====For the stock Syrup====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Bring the [[Sugar|sugar]] and water to the [[Boil|boil]] in a [[Saucepan|saucepan]].\n| Add the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and place the [[Pears|pears]] into the [[Stock|stock]], cover with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]] (make a [[Cartouche|cartouche]]) and [[Simmer|simmer]] until tender.\n| Cool the [[Pears|pears]], cut in half (from top to bottom) and fan them with a knife.  You can cut them in half again to make 8 pieces (which is what I did), but I found it easier to put 6 fans on the tart and just eat the 2 that were left over.  8 pieces can be rather fiddly!\n}}\n====For the Almond Cream====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Cream]] the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] together until pale and fluffy.\n| Gradually add the [[Egg|egg]], the mix in the [[Flour|flour]], [[Ground almonds|ground almonds]] and [[Almond extract|almond extract]].\n}}\n====To assemble====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roll out the [[Pastry|pastry]] and line a greased flan tin with it [use a 20cm (8in) or 23cm (9in) tin] depends on the length of your [[Pears|pears]], as they need to fit from the edge of the pastry case to the centre of the tart.\n| Carefully spread the [[Almond|almond]] [[Cream|cream]] into the [[Pastry|pastry]] case, and then place [[Pears|pears]] on top and lightly press them down.\n| [[Bake]] at 180C / Gas 4 until golden [[Brown|brown]].\n| Allow to cool slightly, and then glaze with hot [[Apricot|apricot]] [[Jam|jam]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Cr\u00e8me Anglaise]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pears #pastry #egg #flour #butter #castersugar #apricot #almondextract #unsaltedbutter #almond #tartebourdaloue </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

(The [[Taste Sensation blue cheese powder]] has a very long shelf life, so I don't need to go shopping for [[Cheese|cheese]] to make the [[Sauce|sauce]]!)\n[[Image:MySampleBlueCheesePowder.jpg|thumb|300px|Taste Sensation Matured Blue Cheese powder|]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 40 g [[Taste Sensation Matured Blue Cheese powder]]\n| 400 ml [[Milk|milk]] (or 4 tablespoons [[Milk powder|milk powder]] & 400ml water - see variations, below)\n| 40 g [[Butter|butter]] - 2 [[Scant|scant]] tablespoons (or [[Olive oil|olive oil]] - I find that preferable)\n| 30 g (2 tbs) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Taste Sensation Matured Blue Cheese powder]] to the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Whisk|whisk]] until combined.  I find it combined better if left for 10 minutes and mixed again, but it seems to work well either way.\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a pan, ensuring it does not burn!\n| Sprinkle the [[Plain flour|plain flour]] over the [[Oil|oil]] and mix into a [[Roux|roux]].\n| Pour in the water and gently [[Simmer|simmer]], stirring well until thickened.  Some say that the [[Milk|milk]] should be introduced bit-by-bit, but I find if you mix it while it heats, it works just as well.\n| Serve - Yum!\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf like me, you are making this during the CV19 'lock-down', we are avoiding going out shopping for [[Milk|milk]] as this introduces another unnecessary ''risk''.  We've fortunately managed to bulk-buy [[Dried milk powder|dried milk powder]]; 4 heaped tablespoons of [[Dried|dried]] [[Milk powder|milk powder]] makes up about 400 ml of milk - perfect for this [[Sauce|sauce]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI've included this in Danish recipes because I know that the [[Taste Sensation]] Blue [[Cheese powder]] is produced from [[Blue cheese|blue cheese]] made in Denmark.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Danish recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#oliveoil #tastesensationmaturedbluecheesepowder #tastesensation #butter #sauce #plainflour #milkpowder #tastesensationmaturedbluecheesesauce #cheesepowder #simmer #tastesensationrecipes</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Spoon the mixture into a lightly greased baking tray.\n| Sprinkle with the remaining [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Brown|brown]] under the [[Grill|grill]].\n}}\n===Variations===\nAdd lots of Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] with the [[Onions|onions]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are struggling to get hold of fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]], at  a push you could add 1 heaped teaspoon of [[dried tarragon]] to a little [[Boiled|boiled]] water, allow it to rehydrate, drain any liquid and then use, however, fresh is plainly better.\n==See also==\n{{Template:Lobster recipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#thermidorsauce #butter #tarragon #parsley #cheese #vegetables #grill #pasta #onions #garlic #blackpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                    {

A great quick meal\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 643\n|PortionCalories = 160\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Truffade recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">If you like cheese...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">...you'll love these  \ud83d\ude0e</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis French-styled dish is traditionally made with Tomme or Cantal [[Cheese|cheese]] but is equally as good made with [[Cheddar]] if you have to.\n\nA great quick meal, supper or even snack.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Olive oil]] or melted [[Butter|butter]] to grease the dish\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) [[Baking|baking]] [[Potatoes|potatoes]] such as Cara, Estima, King Edwards, Marfona, Maris Piper or Vivaldi, '''very''' thinly sliced.\n| 150 g (5 oz) hard [[Cheese|cheese]]; Tomme ([[:Category:Alsace cheeses|Alsace cheeses]], [[:Category:Rh\u00f4ne-Alpes cheeses|Rh\u00f4ne-Alpes cheeses]], [[:Category:Midi-Pyr\u00e9n\u00e9es cheeses|Midi-Pyr\u00e9n\u00e9es cheeses]]), [[:Category:Auvergne cheeses|Cantal]], [[Gruy\u00e8re]] or [[Cheddar]], [[Grated|grated]].\n| Freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 225 g (8 oz) [[Diced|diced]] streaky [[Bacon|bacon]] ([[Lardons|lardons]]) - ''optional''\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grease the base of a shallow [[Baking|baking]] dish or [[Roasting|roasting]] tin.\n| Arrange a layer of [[Onions|onions]] in the base.\n| Top with a layer of [[Potatoes|potatoes]], then a layer of [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| Finish with a final layer of [[Potatoes|potatoes]] topped with [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| Dress with [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and a few dabs of [[Butter|butter]] or [[Oil|oil]].\n| [[Bake]] for 1 hour and ten minutes., remove and allow to rest for 5 minutes\n| If using [[Lardons|lardons]], [[Fry|fry]] them for 4 minutes first and add them in layers with the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Onions|onions]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot, sliced into [[Wedges|wedges]] with a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nSqueeze a bulb or two of [[roasted garlic]] in amongst the potatoes for a really special dish!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potatoes #cheese #truffade #grated #cheddar #butter #nutmeg #onions #lardons #baking #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

-->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1319\n|PortionCalories = 329\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 10 minutes plus chilling time\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Vichyssoise recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Garlic Soup++</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This will sort your colds out!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis chilled [[Leek and potato soup|leek and potato soup]] recipe is not really the standard one, but I think it tastes better!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2-3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 450 g white parts of [[Leeks|leeks]], washed, [[Dried|dried]] and sliced\n| 2 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| 350 g (peeled weight) [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and sliced\n| 1.4 [[Litres|litres]] [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 200 ml thick natural [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n| Seasoning\n| 2-3 tablespoons [[Flat-leaved parsley|flat-leaved parsley]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a deep saucepan.\n| Add the [[Leeks|leeks]] and the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stew|stew]] until they are soft.\n| Add the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and the [[Stock|stock]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and reduce the heat so that it simmers, partially covered, for 45 minutes.\n| Pur\u00e9e, using a stick [[Blender|blender]] or [[Food processor|food processor]].\n| Stir in the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]].\n| Season to taste, but bear in mind that as the [[Soup|soup]] is chilled, you may need to add a little extra [[Salt|salt]].\n| Allow to cool and then chill in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]].\n| Garnish with the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Salad|salad]] as a refreshing [[Light lunch|light lunch]].  Add cro\u00fbtons if you wish.\n===Variations===\nThe more traditional way of making Vichyssoise is to omit the [[Garlic|garlic]], use [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] instead of [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]].  Also [[Cream|cream]] is used instead of [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] and snipped chived instead of [[Parsley|parsley]].\n===Chef's notes===\nTry to get the [[Leeks|leeks]] as dry as possible after washing, otherwise they may [[Steam|steam]] in the [[Oil|oil]], rather than [[Fry|fry]].  If this happens, drain of the liquid and add some more oil.  A hot version of the soup is [[Potage bonne femme (Leek and potato soup)|Potage bonne femme]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:Starters|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Vichysoisse]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vichysoisse #leeks #yoghurt #garlic #potatoes #parsley #vegetablestock #fry #salad #boil #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
